1201 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grabinski


No. 30788


Supreme Court of Washington, Department One


33 Wn.2d 603; 206 P.2d 1022; 1949 Wash. LEXIS 466



May 26, 1949 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court for Yakima County, Washington, which convicted him of selling uncooked meats and groceries on the first day of the week in violation of Wash. Rev. Stat. § 2494 (Remington). He claimed that § 2494 was class legislation and unconstitutional in that it violated U.S. Const. amend. 14, § 1, Wash. Const. art. I, §§ 3, 12, by establishing the first day of the week as a sabbath.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that Wash. Rev. Stat. § 2494 (Remington) was discriminatory because it excepted the sale of certain items from the general prohibition of the sale of personal property on the first day of the week; that it violated religious freedom; that pursuant to Wash. Rev. Stat. § 2496 (Remington), he had a defense because he and his community kept another day as a sabbath; and that he was not allowed to present evidence of community necessity. On review, the court found that: (1) the prohibition of certain activities on the first day of the week had been upheld as a valid exercise of the police power; (2) Wash Rev. Stat. § 2494 (Remington) did not restrict who could sell the designated articles appropriate for sale; (3) § 2494 did not restrict anyone's religious beliefs or practices; and (4) Wash. Rev. Stat. § 2496 (Remington) did not offer a defense to the sale of goods but only to performing labor, so it would not consider the constitutionality of that section.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1202 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dexter


No. 30642


Supreme Court of Washington, Department One


32 Wn.2d 551; 202 P.2d 906; 1949 Wash. LEXIS 386; 13 A.L.R.2d 1081



February 18, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied March 28, 1949.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court for Pend Oreille County (Washington), which upon sustaining a demurrer to the complaint, dismissed an action for injunctive relief brought by the State against appellee landowner.


OVERVIEW: The state forester became aware that the landowner was cutting and removing timber, and directed him to shut down his operations until a permit was obtained. The landowner refused to apply for a permit, and proceedings were instituted by the State enjoining further timber-cutting operations until such time as the landowner should apply for and receive a permit from the state forester, which permit he could not obtain without giving satisfactory assurance that he would comply with 1945 Wash. Laws 193, as amended by 1947 Wash. Laws 218. The trial court held that the statutes were unconstitutional and sustained the demurrer to the complaint. The court held that the statutes were a proper exercise of the police power of the state in that they were designed to provide protection of the natural resources of the state for the better good of the entire population. The court held that the State was entitled to prevail.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1203 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Gilman v. Tax Com


No. 30885


Supreme Court of Washington


32 Wn.2d 480; 202 P.2d 443; 1949 Wash. LEXIS 377



February 4, 1949 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court for Thurston County (Washington), sustaining a demurrer to the complaint, dismissing an action for injunctive relief, upon the taxpayer's complaint against respondents, the State Tax Commission and others, asking that the collection of the tax and the issuance of the bonds by the state finance committee be restrained.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought the action challenging the constitutionality of an initiative measure, which received a favorable vote of the electorate. The complaint asked that the collection of the tax by the state tax commission and the issuance of the bonds by the state finance committee be restrained. On appeal, the court found that the World War I bonds for equalized compensation were brought squarely within Wash. Const. art. VIII, § 3, and contained the provision that each bond should have been made payable at a time not exceeding 20 years from the date of its issuance. Because the initiative measure was explicitly placed outside of Wash. Const. art. VIII, § 3, its proponents said that Wash. Const. art. VIII, § 2 was applicable. The court concluded that the debt to be contracted was not to repel invasion, to suppress insurrection, or to defend the state in war. It follows that the demurrer to the complaint should not have been sustained, and that the taxpayer's complaint should not have been dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1204 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Thys v. State


No. 30281


Supreme Court of Washington


31 Wn.2d 739; 199 P.2d 68; 1948 Wash. LEXIS 307; 81 U.S.P.Q. (BNA) 222



November 4, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Washington sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court for Thurston County (Washington) that found in favor of plaintiff taxpayers in an action to recover business and occupation taxes and retail sales taxes paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers were assessed business and occupation taxes and retail sales taxes, purported to have been levied pursuant to Titles II and III of the Revenue Act of 1935 by the state. The taxpayers paid the assessments, under protest, and filed an action for judgment, contending that the taxes were levied without lawful authority and were illegal. The trial court entered a judgment for the taxpayers. The trial court held that the taxpayers were not subject to the taxes levied against them because they were not doing business in the state of Washington. On appeal, the question before the court for determination was whether the moneys received by the taxpayers, referred to in the contract as "royalties," paid by the respective purchasers of the hop-picking machines, were taxable under the revenue statutes of the state. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the taxpayers were engaged in business practice within the state and were subject to taxation within the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that found in favor of the taxpayers in an action to recover business and occupation taxes and retail sales taxes paid under protest.

 

1205 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Alaska S. S. Co. v. State


No. 30498


Supreme Court of Washington, Department Two


31 Wn.2d 328; 196 P.2d 1001; 1948 Wash. LEXIS 273



August 19, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, state and members of state tax commission, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court for Thurston County (Washington) that was entered in favor of petitioners, domestic steamship company and foreign steamship company, on their action to secure a refund of money paid by the domestic steamship company to the state by way of a sales tax.


OVERVIEW: The domestic steamship company sold a steamship to the foreign steamship company. That steamship was exported to the home country of the foreign steamship company for use in its operations. The state levied a sales tax upon the sale of the steamship and the domestic steamship company paid that tax under protest. Thereafter, petitioners filed an action against respondents to secure a refund of amounts paid as a sales tax. The trial court entered a judgment in favor of petitioners, and respondents appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment that directed a refund in favor of petitioners. The court rested this determination on the basis that the terms of the underlying sale and the actions of the parties clearly indicated that the steamship sold could not have been legally used or operated in waters of the state, except solely as an incident to foreign commerce. Thus, the court concluded that the sale of the steamship constituted a sale of property for export as contemplated by U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 2, and the domestic steamship company's payment of the relevant sales tax was illegal in violation of that constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment that determined that the petitioners were entitled to a refund of certain monies paid to the state as a sales tax was affirmed.

 

1206 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Columbia Steel Co. v. State


No. 30475


Supreme Court of Washington


30 Wn.2d 658; 192 P.2d 976; 1948 Wash. LEXIS 418



May 6, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied September 20, 1948.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the decision of the Superior Court for Thurston County, Washington, which granted the demurrer of respondent, the State, in the taxpayer's action to recover taxes paid.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer paid a deficiency assessed by the State. The deficiency was based upon business and occupation taxes imposed upon persons engaged within the state in the business of making sales at wholesale under Wash. Rev. Stat. § 8370-4 (Remington Supp. 1943) et seq. The trial court dismissed the taxpayer's action to recover the taxes. The taxpayer argued on appeal that the tax was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. art. I, § 8 because it imposed a burden on interstate commerce. The court agreed and reversed. The court found that 40 per cent of the business on which the assessment was based was done upon contracts negotiated, made, and concluded outside the state. The only thing that transpired in the state was the delivery of products to various customers by common carriers. The court held that the deficiency assessment was based upon a tax upon amounts derived from business that the State was prohibited from taxing under the federal constitution. The court held that the tax was invalid because it constituted state interference with the freedom of interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded with instructions to the trial court to overrule the State's demurrer.

 

1207 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Swanson v. Perham


No. 30456


Supreme Court of Washington, Department Two


30 Wn.2d 368; 191 P.2d 689; 1948 Wash. LEXIS 391



March 29, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minority stockholders challenged the judgment of the Superior Court for Yakima County (Washington), which dismissed appellants' action to compel recognition of the right of cumulative voting claimed by them.


OVERVIEW: The corporation whose stockholders' voting rights are here involved, was organized in 1919, under the general corporation laws of the state of Washington. The by-laws provided that each stockholder should be entitled to cast one vote for each share of stock standing in his name on the books. Appellants claimed the right to cast their votes cumulatively at a meeting to elect officers. The chairman ruled that the only permissible method of voting was that of straight voting. The court held that the right of a stockholder to vote for directors was a valuable vested property right arising out of the contract of incorporation, and it was therefore a right saved and protected by § 63 of the Uniform Business Corporation Act. That right was not impaired or affected by § 28(3), for to deprive the stockholder of such right was to deprive him of an essential attribute of his property. Section § 28(3) of the Act, relating to cumulative voting, did not apply and hence did not divest the majority stockholders of their vested right to elect all of the directors of the corporation by the straight voting method.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1208 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Robinson v. Fluent


No. 30523


Supreme Court of Washington


30 Wn.2d 194; 191 P.2d 241; 1948 Wash. LEXIS 381



March 18, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied May 14, 1948.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state, on the relation of an individual (relator), applied for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent state treasurer to pay a warrant. Intervenor state pension fund also resisted the application for a writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: The state applied for a writ of mandamus to compel the state treasurer to pay a warrant drawn by the state auditor on the treasurer in to pay relator for services rendered to a joint legislative fact-finding committee, created by a concurrent resolution of the legislature. The concurrent resolution expressly authorized the committee to sit after adjournment of the legislature. The treasurer demurred to the application and filed a motion seeking the denial of the application on the basis that the legislature was without constitutional authority to establish by concurrent resolution any committee to function after adjournment sine die of that legislature and that no valid appropriation existed from which to pay the relator's warrant. The court issued the writ, holding that the legislature possessed the inherent power to investigate and that there was no constitutional restriction on the legislature's power to establish, by a concurrent resolution, an investigatory committee to function after adjournment of the legislature. Thus, the concurrent resolution creating the committee was an authorized act of the legislature and was effective for the purposes for which it was adopted.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the issuance of a writ of mandamus compelling the treasury to pay the warrant, in an application by the state, on behalf of the relater, to obtain such a writ.

 

1209 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Berger v. Sailors Union of Pac.


No. 30277


Supreme Court of Washington


29 Wn.2d 810; 189 P.2d 473; 1948 Wash. LEXIS 462; 21 L.R.R.M. 2448; 14 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P64,380



February 13, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, members of an alleged limited partnership, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court for King County, Washington, which found in favor of respondents, a labor organization (union) and its members, in the partnership's action for injunctive relief. The partnership brought the action to enjoin the union from picketing the partnership's motorship and from hindering any person from transacting business with the partnership.


OVERVIEW: When the partnership brought their motorship alongside a wharf to be loaded with freight for another trip, the union established a picket line. The partnership's longshoremen refused to cross the picket line to continue loading the ship. The partnership contended that it was a limited partnership, in which one individual was the general partner and the crewmembers were the limited partners. The union contended that the partnership was a mere sham, and that the monthly drawing accounts were in fact wages of the limited partners. The trial court denied the application for an injunction. On appeal, the court found that the relationship was a usual employment relationship of master and servant. The court noted that it was the purpose of the picketing to persuade the partnership from entering into an agreement with the union so that there could be a union delegate on the motorship. The court further noted that there was no evidence of violence. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because there was a valid labor dispute at issue and that an injunction would not lie to prohibit the union and its members from peacefully picketing the partnership's motorship.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1210 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Vine St. Comm'l v. City of Marysville


NO. 42206-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


98 Wn. App. 541; 989 P.2d 1238; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 2133



December 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied July 12 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wn. LEXIS 436.
Reconsideration denied by Vine St. Commer. Pshp. v. City of Marysville, 1999 Wn. App. LEXIS 2214 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 20, 1999)
Review denied by Vine St. Commer. Pshp. v. City of Marysville, 141 Wn.2d 1006, 10 P.3d 1075, 2000 Wash. LEXIS 436 (2000)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Vine St. Commer. P'ship v. City of Marysville, 118 Wn. App. 1027, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2526 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) granting defendant's motion for summary judgment dismissing plaintiffs' claim for damages resulting from defendant's wrongful denial of utility services.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were property owners outside the city limits of defendant city that paid an assessment for sewer mains and then applied for utility services. However, defendant denied the application because plaintiffs applied for annexation to a neighboring city instead of defendant as required by local ordinance. Utility service was eventually established for plaintiffs and plaintiffs brought an action for damages resulting from the delays in supplying utility service. The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment and plaintiffs appealed. On appeal, the court stated that plaintiffs were required to follow the ordinance requiring them to apply for annexation with defendant. However, the court also stated that, since plaintiffs paid the assessment for the sewer main, plaintiffs had acquired an enforceable right that defendants denied. Furthermore, the court found that the application of the ordinance operated as an unconstitutional impairment of contract. Consequently, the trial court was reversed.


OUTCOME: Judgment granting defendant's motion for summary judgment was reversed because defendant unconstitutionally impaired plaintiffs' contract.

 

1211 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


First Healthcare Corp. v. Department of Soc. & Health Servs.


No. 23734-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 2119



December 17, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 11, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wn. LEXIS 415.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 98 Wn. App. 1033.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 94-2-00470-8. Date filed: 08/14/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Gary D. Tabor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for entry of judgment in favor of Department.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged judgment of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) reversing a decision granting appellant Department of Social and Health Services a refund from respondents licensed nursing home facilities for non-Medicaid costs from certain reimbursement rates paid to respondents.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Department of Social and Health Services retroactively excluded non-Medicaid costs from certain reimbursement rates paid to respondents, licensed nursing home facilities, for two years. By reducing these past rates, appellant sought a refund from respondents. In reversing superior court's judgment for respondents, court of appeals held respondents were entitled to receive reimbursement only for Medicaid costs and it was error for respondents to submit an estimate for reimbursement that included non-Medicaid costs. The court held that appellant made a timely, lawful retroactive rate adjustment and no constitutional principles were violated because respondents knew, even before the period in question, that they were not entitled to reimbursement for non-Medicaid expenses. Because manner of computing the rate was not in accord with appellant's rules, error occurred in the cost reports that were submitted by respondents; and appellant erred by accepting respondents' cost reports in setting the rates and by failing to discover the erroneous reporting.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed and remanded where appellant Department of Social and Health Services made a timely, lawful retroactive rate adjustment and no constitutional principles were violated because respondents, licensed nursing home facilities, knew, even before the period in question, that they were not entitled to reimbursement for non-Medicaid expenses.

 

1212 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Isla Verde Int'l v. City of Camas


No. 23225-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


99 Wn. App. 127; 990 P.2d 429; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 2219



December 17, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals February 11, 2000.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted September 5, 2000, Reported at: 141 Wn.2d 1011, 10 P.3d 1071, 2000 Wash. LEXIS 523. As Amended on Denial of Reconsideration February 11, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 268.


PRIOR HISTORY: Previously Reported at: 99 Wn. App. 127, 990 P.2d 429.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington) which found that the secondary road requirement it imposed upon respondent developer violated due process and Wash. Rev. Code § 64.40, and that the open space set-aside ordinance provided for an unconstitutional taking.


OVERVIEW: Respondent developer challenged appellant city's open-space set-aside ordinance and a city requirement that it construct a secondary access road as a condition of approval for its subdivision application. The court agreed with the trial court that the set-aside ordinance violated the Takings Clause of U.S. Const. amend. V because there was no evidence that the ordinance was roughly proportional to the impact of the proposed development. The court found that the record indicated that legitimate fire safety concerns led to the secondary road requirement and that the road was reasonably necessary for public safety. The court held that respondent failed to show that the secondary road requirement was unduly oppressive and did not demonstrate that the government action was arbitrary, irrational, or tainted by improper motive. The court found that the trial court erred in concluding that the secondary road requirement constituted a violation of due process. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling regarding the set-aside ordinance, but reversed the ruling regarding the road requirement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the judgment declaring that appellant city's secondary road requirement violated the Fifth Amendment and city statute. The court affirmed that part of the judgment declaring that the 30 percent set-aside ordinance, as applied to respondent developer, was unconstitutional.

 

1213 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Inland Foundry Co. v. Spokane County Air Pollution Control Auth.


No. 18138-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FOUR


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 2024



November 30, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 12 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wn. LEXIS 438.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 95-2-02114-4. Date filed: 12/07/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Salvatore F. Cozza.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foundry company appealed from Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington) decision affirming summary judgment granted by Pollution Control Hearings Board in favor of defendant county air pollution control authority in action related to plaintiff's violations of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 70.94.141,.151 and Wash. Admin. Code § 173-400-105.


OVERVIEW: After defendant county air pollution control authority gave plaintiff foundry company written notice of its violations of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 70.94.141,.151 and Wash. Admin. Code § 173-400-105, plaintiff appealed to the pollution control hearings board (board). The board granted defendant's summary judgment motion. The superior court affirmed and plaintiff appealed. On appeal, the court rejected plaintiff's argument that power to perform routine administrative functions is restricted to a quorum of the board of directors. The court also rejected plaintiff's constitutional challenge of Spokane County Air Pollution Control Authority Reg. I, art. IV, §§ 4.01, 4.02 because those regulations do not involve First Amendment concerns. Finally, the court rejected plaintiff's contention that defendant violated section 70.94.151 when it failed to make an individual determination that plaintiff was a pollution source. Because the statute does not contemplate consideration on a case-by-case basis, defendant was not required to justify the fee by individually assessing the effects of plaintiff's emissions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed; under state law, county air pollution control board was not required to justify the fee it imposed upon plaintiff by individually assessing the health, economic and social effects of plaintiff's emissions.

 

1214 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Inland Foundry Co. v. Spokane County Air Pollution Control Auth.


No. 18137-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FOUR


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 2025



November 30, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 95-2-02110-1. Date filed: 12/07/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Salvatore F. Cozza.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington) affirming the Pollution Control Hearings Board's dismissal of appellant's challenge of respondent's order.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Spokane County Air Pollution Control Authority approved appellant's notice of construction and application for approval for the installation of furnaces and emissions control equipment (NOC), with conditions. When respondent inspected appellant, it found that emissions were being vented into the outside air, thus it issued a notice of violation and an enforcement order. Appellant challenged the dismissal of its appeal of the order. The court found that, to the extent appellant was challenging the NOC, there was no fact material to the appeal for respondent to dispute. To the extent that appellant was challenging the agency action, the burden was on it to prove respondent did not follow the required inspection procedures. Until it did so, respondent need not prove its order was lawful. Further, the court found appellant's appeal was frivolous, so it awarded attorney fees to respondent.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. To the extent that appellant was challenging the order to comply with the approved notice of construction and an application for approval, the burden was on it to prove respondent did not follow the required inspection procedures. Until it did so, respondent did not need to prove its order was lawful.

 

1215 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sims


No. 42233-2-I/Consolid.w/No. 42259-6-I, No. 42259-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 2017



November 29, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petitions for Review Denied May 4, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wash. LEXIS 374.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-1-00953-3. Date filed: 02/09/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Faith Ireland.
State v. Sims, 98 Wn. App. 1018, 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 3790 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of their convictions in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) for second-degree felony murder and manslaughter in the first degree, alleging trial court error in refusing to instruct on defense of another, prosecutorial misconduct, ineffectiveness of counsel, and insufficient evidence to prove first-degree manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, twin brothers, fought with victim. Victim threatened to kill appellants' parents and sister, who were not present but lived nearby. Appellant retrieved handgun from car and fired two shots in direction of victim, killing him. Appellants were convicted, one for second-degree felony murder and the other for manslaughter in first degree. On appeal, the court affirmed. Appellant was not entitled to self-defense instruction because reasonable person could not have perceived imminent threat of great bodily harm to parents and sister; prosecutorial misconduct through improper remarks was not so flagrant that prejudice could not have been cured by appellant's counsel through request for appropriate instruction that jury was not to draw any adverse inference; failure of appellant's counsel to object to prosecutorial misconduct was not incompetence justifying reversal because it involved nonessential testimony; and evidence was sufficient to support accomplice liability, since respondent showed appellant had general knowledge of crime.


OUTCOME: Convictions were affirmed, because prosecutorial misconduct was not so flagrant that resulting prejudice could not have been cured by appropriate instruction.

 

1216 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. West


No. 41735-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1984



November 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 12, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wn. LEXIS 440.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-1-06305-8. Date filed: 11/17/1997. Judge signing: Hon. Larry Jordan.



DISPOSITION: Exceptional sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which imposed an exceptional sentence on appellant after she struck and killed a pedestrian and pled guilty to vehicular homicide, felony hit and run, reckless driving, and reckless endangerment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to charges of vehicular homicide, felony hit and run, reckless driving, and reckless endangerment after she struck and killed a pedestrian while driving under the influence of alcohol. The trial court imposed an exceptional sentence of 108 months on the vehicular homicide charge, setting forth three aggravating factors on which the exceptional sentence was based. The factors included appellant's extraordinarily high blood alcohol content, appellant's particularized knowledge about the dangers of drunk driving, and the victim's pedestrian status. The court affirmed. The court rejected appellant's argument that because vehicular homicide and reckless driving charges were the same criminal conduct, they should not have been counted separately. The court also rejected appellant's vagueness challenge, holding that a person of reasonable understanding could comprehend that Washington's Sentencing Reform Act authorized a sentencing court, in its discretion, to impose an exceptional sentence based on conduct more egregious than typical.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed judgment of trial court, holding that exceptional sentence was appropriate in light of aggravating factors.

 

1217 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gosho


No. 40988-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1988



November 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 97-1-00023-2. Date filed: 07/21/1997. Judge signing: Hon. Gerald L. Knight.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment from Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) imposing an exceptional sentence after he was convicted of first-degree reckless endangerment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his friends were involved in an argument with another group of males at a mall. Shortly thereafter, appellant's friend drove by the mall food court, and appellant started shooting toward the heavily populated area. A jury found him guilty of first-degree reckless endangerment, and the court imposed an exceptional sentence on four different bases. Appellant contended that three of the trial court's bases were not legally adequate. There was no evidence to contradict the trial court's statement that any one basis would have resulted in the same exceptional sentence. Therefore, the appellate court held that the trial court could impose the exceptional sentence solely on the unchallenged fact that appellant's crime involved multiple acts and multiple victims. Additionally, the court found no merit in appellant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel and constitutional challenges to the Sentencing Reform Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.010.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed judgment and sentence where the trial court's exceptional sentence could be imposed on the unchallenged ground that the crime involved multiple acts and multiple victims.

 

1218 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


No. 42208-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1993



November 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-1-03370-1. Date filed: 02/23/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Brian D. Gain.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment from Superior Court of King County (Washington) convicting him on a jury verdict of robbery in the first degree, unlawful imprisonment, and assault in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Appellant approached victim at a bus stop and prevented him from boarding the bus. Appellant hit the victim, knocked him down, took his gold chain and wallet, and kicked him until a police officer approached. A jury convicted him of robbery in the first degree, unlawful imprisonment, and assault in the first degree. On appeal, appellant contended that there was insufficient evidence to support the first-degree assault conviction and that the trial court should have counted the three offenses as the same criminal conduct for sentencing purposes. The court held there was ample evidence of injury to support the conviction. The court held appellant's failure to raise the issue of same criminal conduct in the trial court did not preclude appellate review of that issue. Finding that the robbery and the unlawful imprisonment offenses involved the same criminal intent and conduct, the court remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed convictions where they were supported by substantial evidence. Court remanded for resentencing where the robbery and the unlawful imprisonment offenses involved the same criminal intent and, therefore, constituted the same criminal conduct.

State v. Schloredt


No. 43569-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


97 Wn. App. 789; 987 P.2d 647; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1878



November 1, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the Superior Court of King County's (Washington) conviction of burglary in the second degree and of four counts of possession of stolen property in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: When appellant was apprehended in a convenience store stealing cigarettes, he had stolen credit cards in his pocket. Appellant was convicted of burglary in the second degree and of possession of stolen property (specifically, stolen "access devices") in the second degree. On appeal, appellant argued that there was insufficient evidence to establish all elements of the possession of stolen property charges under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.56.160. Appellant also asserted that he had received insufficient notice of the possession of stolen property charges because respondent state used the term "credit card" instead of "access device" in its information. The court affirmed appellant's conviction, reasoning that the jury had sufficient evidence to conclude that the cards met the statutory definition of "access device." Furthermore, although the information used the term "credit card," appellant had sufficient notice of the charges against him because it referenced the specific statutory provision in its information.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. The jury had sufficient evidence to conclude that the credit cards met the statutory definition of "access device." Although the information used the term "credit card" instead of "access device," appellant had sufficient notice of the charges against him because it referenced the applicable statutory provision.

Wings of the World v. Small Claims


NO. 43775-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


97 Wn. App. 803; 987 P.2d 642; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1879



November 1, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Small claims court appellant challenged Superior Court of King County (Washington) decision denying appellant's petition for extraordinary writ seeking review of constitutionality of small claims court procedures.


OVERVIEW: Small claims court appellant challenged general jurisdiction court's decision denying appellant's petition for extraordinary writ seeking review of the constitutionality of small claims court procedures. Appellant did not have a right to jury trial under Wash. Const. art. I, § 21, because, at common law at the time the constitution was adopted, there was an exception to the jury trial right for small monetary claims. Small claims statutory appeals bond and filing fee requirements did not conflict with rules of appeal, unconstitutionally discriminate against indigent appellants, or infringe on appellant's right of access to appellate courts; the requirements were rationally related to the legitimate state goal of providing an inexpensive and conclusive determination of small claims, and were thus not unconstitutional. Appellant did not have a right to be heard by an elected, as opposed to a pro tem, judge. General jurisdiction court's denial of writ affirmed.


OUTCOME: General jurisdiction court's denial of writ affirmed; appellant did not have right to jury trial or to be heard by elected, as opposed to pro tem, judge, and appeals bond and filing fee requirements did not conflict with appellate rules, unconstitutionally discriminate or infringe on appellant's access to appellate courts.

State v. Harris


No. 40004-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


97 Wn. App. 647; 985 P.2d 417; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1752



October 4, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, deaf sex offender, appealed Superior Court of Snohomish County's (Washington) revocation of his suspended sentence, claiming that failure to provide a signing interpreter during meetings with probation officer violated Wash. Rev. Code §42.120(3) and his due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a deaf man who pled guilty to a sex offense, was given a Special Sexual Offender Sentencing Alternative (SSOSA) but later violated conditions of that sentence. The court revoked his suspended sentence. Appellant argued that the court's failure to provide a signing interpreter during probation meetings violated both state statute and his due process rights. The court found that Wash. Rev. Code §42.120(3), which required signing interpreters for criminal suspects, violated Wash. Const. art. II, § 19 because it embraced more than one subject and did not give the public notice of the signing interpreter requirement. The court also found appellant was able to read and his intelligence was normal, and his own actions in initially complying with the conditions of his SSOSA defeated his argument that without an interpreter he did not have adequate notice of what he was required to do. He was not denied due process.


OUTCOME: The lower court's judgment was affirmed because the statute requiring signing interpreters was unconstitutional and appellant was not denied due process by the lack of an interpreter because he understood the requirements of his probation.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted criminal defendant, challenged his convictions for second degree assault with a deadly weapon and unlawful possession of a firearm entered in the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington). The court consolidated appellant's personal restraint petition with the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued for reversal of his convictions on the grounds that the state was allowed to amend its counts to add charges, the evidence did not support the verdict, his jury instructions were not given, the crimes should have been consolidated, he received ineffective service of counsel, his sentence was improperly enhanced, and, in a petition of personal restraint, that unconstitutional prejudice was shown. 1226 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Furfaro v. City of Seattle


NO. 43409-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


97 Wn. App. 537; 984 P.2d 1055; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1731; 28 Media L. Rep. 1206



September 27, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which issued judgment for appellees in appellants' claim for damages against appellees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were arrested without a warrant for violation of Seattle, Wash., Mun. Code 6.270.100 (SMC 6.270.100) for topless dancing. After one of appellants was acquitted, appellants sued appellees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court reversed. The police should have obtained a warrant before arresting appellants for violation of SMC 6.270.100. Non-obscene nude dancing was entitled to U.S. Const. amend. I protection. SMC 6.270.100 was constitutional only because of the non-obscene dance exception therein. Before the police can make an arrest there must be an assessment that the performance, as a whole, was not protected under that exception. The police could not instantly make this type of assessment and therefore were required to obtain a warrant after probable cause was determined. Arresting nude dancers without a warrant and before determining such performances were obscene was an unconstitutional prior restraint that violated U.S. Const. amends. I and IV.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision, finding appellees' warrantless arrest of appellants for violation of an ordinance that banned stage dancers from sexual self-touching was unconstitutional because appellees were required to obtain a judicial determination of probable cause in which a court could determine whether the dancers' conduct was obscene.

Swoboda v. Town of La Conner


No. 43192-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


97 Wn. App. 613; 987 P.2d 103; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1653



September 13, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported in Table Case Format at: 97 Wn. App. 1032.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment of the Superior court of Skagit County (Washington) in which the court denied appellant's permit applications under the Land Use Petition Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.130.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought to demolish or relocate two buildings, remove 10 trees, and relocate two trees in respondent's historic preservation district, in order to construct a building. The trial court affirmed the administrative decision denying appellant's permit applications under the Land Use Petition Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.130, because it contended demolition or relocation of the existing structures was inconsistent with the La Conner, Wa., Code § 15.50.080. On appeal, appellant asserted §15.50.080(2) was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that, when a challenged ordinance involved land use regulation, the ordinance was judged as applied, not evaluated for facial vagueness. Additionally, an ordinance had to contain ascertainable standards for adjudication in order to limit discretionary enforcement of the law. The court reviewed § 15.50.080 and determined it provided detailed and technical standards, as well as design review criteria, and therefore was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision and concluded that certain sections of the La Conner Municipal Code were not unconstitutionally vague, the Hearing Examiner had jurisdiction to hear the appeal, appellant was not denied his due process rights, and the hearings did not violate the appearance of fairness doctrine.

State v. Austin (in Re Austin)


Cons. No. 21267-6-II, No. 23975-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1652



September 10, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 97 Wn. App. 1029.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 95-1-01839-4. Date filed: 09/18/1996. Judge signing: Hon. Robert L. Harris.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, after being convicted of first-degree attempted child molestation in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.44.083 and 9A.28.020 and being sentenced as a persistent offender by the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington), attacked his sentence through counsel and attacked the underlying conviction in a pro se brief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of attempted first-degree child molestation in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.44.083 and 9A.28.020, was sentenced as a persistent offender. Appellant attacked his sentence through counsel and his underlying conviction in a pro se brief. The appellate court affirmed the decision of the trial court and denied appellant's petition. Appellant's persistent-offender status was properly supported by his earlier robbery conviction because appellant did not have a right to contest a prior conviction at his subsequent sentencing for another offense. Appellant's persistent-offender sentence was not cruel or unusual punishment and did not violate constitutional double-jeopardy protections because the imposed sentence was legislatively authorized based on the severity of the underlying offense. Appellant's attempted child molestation conviction was supported by sufficient evidence and he was not denied his U.S. Const. VI right to effective counsel assistance because counsel's performance was sufficient and was not prejudicial.


OUTCOME: In affirming the trial court's decision and denying appellant's petition, the appellate court held that sentencing appellant as a persistent offender was properly supported by his earlier robbery conviction and was not cruel or unusual punishment or impermissible double jeopardy. Appellant was adequately represented by counsel and was not prejudiced by counsel's performance.

State v. Homer


No. 17617-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1640



September 9, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 97 Wn. App. 1028.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Lincoln County. Docket No: 98-1-00018-7. Date filed: 06/22/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Richard W. Miller.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the calculation of his offender score and the imposition of the exceptional sentence by the Superior Court of Lincoln County (Washington), where he was convicted of two counts of third-degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of third-degree assault. A jury found him guilty on both counts. A presentence investigation report indicated defendant had previously been convicted of seven felonies, three as a juvenile and four as an adult. He also had 12 prior misdemeanor convictions and seven community placement violations. Lower court imposed an exceptional sentence. Defendant appealed. Defendant failed to show that his prior juvenile convictions were unconstitutional and state established those convictions by a preponderance of the evidence. Lower court did not err by including the three prior juvenile felony convictions in his criminal history. The calculation of his offender score was therefore correct. Court also noted defendant had an extensive misdemeanor criminal history that was not used in calculating his offender score. Four of defendant's misdemeanor convictions were a form of assault. Thus, the lower court did not err by determining his misdemeanor history resulted in a sentence that was too lenient. The imposition of the exceptional sentence was justified.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed the sentence imposed on defendant since the lower court did not err by including defendant's three prior juvenile felony convictions in his criminal history for the calculation of his offender score and the imposition of the exceptional sentence was justified given defendant's extensive misdemeanor history.

State v. Twyman


No. 42506-4-I consolidated with: No. 42916-7-I, No. 42958-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


98 Wn. App. 508; 983 P.2d 703; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1625



September 7, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the Superior Court of King County's (Washington) denial of their motion to have the jury pools in their criminal trials drawn from the entire county.


OVERVIEW: Respondent charged each of the appellants with crimes. Prior to trial, defense counsel moved to have the jury pools drawn from the entirety of King County. Appellants argued that the zip code zone method or other area jury pool process used was improper even if seemingly authorized by Wash. Rev. Code § 2.36.050. To the extent this selection of the jury pool was to be allowed, appellants argued that the statute was unconstitutional or was not substantially complied with. The motions were denied. The court noted that Wash. Rev. Code § 2.36.050 permitted courts of limited jurisdiction to select jury panels from the population of the area served by the court. The court found that the statute conformed to state constitutional requirements that guaranteed criminal defendants the right to trial before a "jury of the county."


OUTCOME: The denial of appellants' motion was affirmed, because the current jury pool process was in conformity with constitutional standards guaranteeing criminal appellants the right to trial by a jury of the county.

State v. Petz


No. 42209-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1565



August 30, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 97 Wn. App. 1010.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-1-08397-1. Date filed: 02/23/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Richard M. Ishikawa.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him for felony stalking. The appellant contended that his posting of flyers about his estranged wife was a "constitutionally protected activity" and that admission of his prior bad acts was prejudicial and irrelevant.


OVERVIEW: The appellant was convicted of felony stalking after he made repeated calls and threats, and posted flyers seeking information on the activities of his estranged wife. The appellant had a long history of threatening both his wife and child. The appellant challenged his conviction on the grounds that his posting of flyers was a "constitutionally protected activity", and that the lower court's admission of his prior bad acts was prejudicial and irrelevant. The court affirmed the appellant's conviction. The court held that although posting flyers was normally a constitutionally protected activity, as practiced by the appellant, it was directed at intimidating and threatening his wife. The court also upheld the lower court's admission of the appellant's prior bad acts. The court found that because the felony stalking statute had an element of "objective fear", the evidence was necessary to prove that the victim's fear of the appellant was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellant's conviction for felony stalking. The court found that although posting flyers was a normally constitutionally protected activity, as practiced by the appellant, it was intended to intimidate and harass his wife. The court also found that evidence of the appellant's prior bad acts was admissible to prove the objective "reasonable fear" element of felony harassment and stalking.

Melgin v. City of Issaquah


No. 44130-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1597



August 30, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 97 Wn. App. 1017.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-2-18126-1. Date filed: 12/24/1997. Judge signing: Hon. Glenna S. Hall.



DISPOSITION: Summary dismissal of Bacons' damages claims affirmed and ruling that rezoning ordinance is void for vagueness reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a Superior Court of King County (Washington) decision that although appellants' property had been subjected to a property use restriction that was unconstitutionally vague, they were denied damages under claims of violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, Wash. Rev. Code § 64.40, and for reverse condemnation. Respondent city cross-appealed order directing it to issue a business license and court's denial of attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Respondent adopted a new land use code, and appellants' property was zoned for retail use; however, a prior property use agreement (PUA) severely limited appellants' property use. Appellants entered into a sale agreement with prospective purchasers, contingent on the removal of the restrictions. City denied prospective purchasers' application for a license to operate a retail store, based on the PUA, and a hearing officer affirmed. Superior court held the section of the zoning ordinance restricting appellants' property use was void for vagueness, but denied request for damages. Appellate court stated the appeal was timely filed; however, ordinance not unconstitutionally vague. It was clear and readily understandable that a PUA was in effect. Because ordinance was not vague, arguments appellants were due damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was meritless. Respondent did not arbitrarily deny the license when the decision was based on a duly enacted ordinance, nor was respondent's PUA a taking of property. Lastly, superior court did not abuse its discretion in denying attorney's fees to respondent, and order requiring it to issue license was moot by subsequently enacted ordinance.


OUTCOME: Decision that appellants' property subjected to an unconstitutionally vague use restriction was reversed. Ordinance was clear and readily understandable. Because ordinance was not vague, appellants were not due damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, nor was license arbitrarily denied or property taken. No abuse of discretion occurred in denying respondent its attorney's fees, and order requiring it issue license was moot.

In re Pers. Restraint of Quinn


No. 43503-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1517



August 23, 1999, Filed

Appeal after remand at State v. Quinn, 119 Wn. App. 1009, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3302 (2003)



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Quinn's personal restraint petition granted, and his case remanded to trial court with instruction to vacate his felony murder conviction and sentence him for his first degree murder conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner convict filed a personal restraint petition seeking relief from his convictions for first degree premeditated murder and second degree felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner shot and killed victim after an exchange of words. Petitioner was charged with first degree murder for killing victim with premeditated intent, and with second degree murder for killing victim while committing or attempting to commit a second degree assault. Petitioner was found guilty of both crimes, and his challenges to his convictions on appeal, which related to the trial court's refusal to admit evidence of threats on his life, failed. Petitioner filed a personal restraint petition seeking relief from his convictions. Petitioner argued, among other things, that his two convictions based upon one homicide violated the double jeopardy clauses of the state and federal constitutions. Therefore, petitioner contended, one of the convictions had to be vacated. The court agreed, vacating his conviction for second degree felony murder vacated. Petitioner was protected under U.S. Const. amend V and Wash. Const. art. I, § 9 against multiple punishments for the same offense.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's personal restraint petition was granted and petitioner's case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate his felony murder conviction and to sentence him for his first degree murder conviction. Convictions for both first degree premeditated murder and second degree felony murder violated the constitutional prohibition against double jeopardy.

State v. Williams


No. 40333-8-I/40338-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1519



August 23, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 29, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wash. LEXIS 150. Reported in Table Case Format at: 97 Wn. App. 1002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 93-1-04778-5. Date filed: 03/03/1997. Judge signing: Hon. Michael S. Spearman.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brothers appealed a judgment on retrial from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted them of second degree felony murder, on the grounds that they had been denied their constitutional right to confrontation under U.S. Cons. amend. VI and that it was error to refuse to sever their criminal trial.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court affirmed defendant brothers' criminal convictions, finding that each defendant's statement corroborated the nontestifying codefendant's statement against him. The appellate court noted that the sole difference in the testimonies was not a critical detail, given the crime with which defendants were charged. The appellate court concluded that admission of the statements did not pose a problem under U.S. Cons. amend. VI and severance was not mandated where the similarity in the statements rendered harmless any error and each codefendant's confession was reliable as an "interlocking" confession. The appellate court further found that there was no abuse of discretion in denying the motion to sever on the basis of mutually antagonistic defense, noting that each defendant presented the same defense to the jury and neither defendant demonstrated such manifest prejudice as to warrant discretionary severance. The appellate court declined the address the argument that the felony murder rule application was unconstitutional, concluding that binding precedent indicated that the rule was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the criminal convictions, finding that defendant brothers' right to confrontation had not been violated and it was not error to refuse to sever their trial where each codefendant's statement was reliable as an "interlocking" confession, the similarity between the statements rendered harmless any error found in the testimony, and defendants showed no manifest prejudice from the failure to sever.

In re Interest of Skinner

August 23, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision of Superior Court of King County (Washington) terminating his parental rights to allow adoption of his son through respondent agency.


OVERVIEW: Mother of minor child requested the placement of the child for adoption through respondent agency. Appellant father did not consent and appealed the decision to terminate his parental rights. Appellant argued that both federal and state constitutions, under the Due Process, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Wash. Const. art. I, § 3, and Equal Protection clauses, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, required the state to offer remedial services prior to termination. The court held that this was not a dependency proceeding, with a goal of reuniting parent and child, and thus no remedial services were required. In affirming the decision, the court found clear and cogent evidence that appellant had failed to perform his parental duties and that he had no realistic plan for caring for the child. Appellant had failed to make reasonable efforts to demonstrate his willingness to support his child with the resources available to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to terminate plaintiff father's parental rights as there was clear, cogent, and convincing evidence that he had had failed to perform his parental duties under circumstances showing a lack of regard for his parental obligations.

Skokomish Indian Tribe v. Fitzsimmons


No. 23367-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


97 Wn. App. 84; 982 P.2d 1179; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1509



August 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied January 5, 2000, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 227, 970 P.2d 731, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 70.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Skokomish Indian Tribe, sought review of a Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) decision that its petition was moot. Appellant's petition sought review of respondent Washington Department of Ecology's letter to the Federal Energy Regulatory Commission stating that although a dam project did not comply with the Washington Coastal Zone Program, respondent declined to object to the licensing of it.


OVERVIEW: The City of Tacoma applied to the Federal Energy Regulatory Commission (FERC) for licensing of a dam project, and appellant, the Skokomish Indian Tribe, actively participated as an interested party. Respondent, the Washington State Department of Ecology, declared that although the project did not comply with Washington's Coastal Zone Program, it would decline to object to it and FERC issued the requested license. Appellant sought review of that decision, and trial court dismissed their petition as moot. Appellate court reversed. Although a state court could not provide direct relief to appellant because it had no authority to directly order FERC to reconsider its licensing decision, a state court judgment in appellant's favor would enable review of FERC's licensing of the project, and thus the court could provide effective relief. In addition, state court was the correct forum for challenging a state agency's decision. Lastly, respondent's decision was arbitrary and capricious because it explicitly acknowledged that it was inconsistent with state law, and appellant was not precluded from judicial review where it was not required under state law to seek administrative review.


OUTCOME: Decision that appellant's petition was moot was reversed because a state court judgment in appellant's favor would enable review of Federal Energy Regulatory Commission licensing of a dam project, and thus the court could provide effective relief. In addition, court held respondent's decision was arbitrary and capricious because it explicitly acknowledged that it was inconsistent with state law.

State v. Gilmer


No. 16666-0-III, No. 17605-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


96 Wn. App. 875; 981 P.2d 902; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1461



August 10, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied February 8, 2000, Reported at: 139 Wn.2d 1023, 994 P.2d 848, 2000 Wash. LEXIS 117.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Yakima County Superior Court (Washington) for second-degree felony murder arguing that the application of the felony murder rule violated his Eighth Amendment rights.


OVERVIEW: The information alleged that defendant caused the death of another in the course of and furtherance of the crime of malicious mischief and or reckless endangerment. Defendant fired a bullet into a car that he thought was empty. The bullet struck a passenger and killed him. Defendant was charged by information with second-degree murder by commission of a felony. The use of a deadly weapon during the crime was added to the allegation. A jury found defendant guilty of second-degree murder and added the deadly weapons enhancement. The parties agreed that the standard range for the crime, including the firearm enhancement, was 183 to 224 months in prison and the court imposed a sentence of 17 years and 8 months. Defendant appealed, challenging the operation of the felony murder rule. Defendant argued that a conviction for felony murder was proper only when death was a foreseeable consequence of the predicate crime. The court noted that intent to kill was not an element of second-degree felony murder. Defendant's conviction and sentence was affirmed because the purpose of the felony murder statute was to punish those who committed a homicide in the course of a felony.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for second-degree felony murder was affirmed because although the felony murder rule was harsh, it served the legislature's intent to punish those who commit murder during the course of a felony.

State v. Gregory


No. 42977-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1467



August 9, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 29, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wash. LEXIS 158.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 97-1-01087-4. Date filed: 06/12/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Ronald L. Castleberry.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant minor challenged judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which sentenced defendant, under an exceptional sentencing standard, to 60 months incarceration pursuant to his convictions for first-degree manslaughter and unlawful imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction for first-degree manslaughter and unlawful imprisonment, criminal defendant minor argued that the trial court erred in imposing a 60-month exceptional sentence based on disputed facts that were contained only in an affidavit of probable cause. The court acknowledged that the trial court was restricted to relying only on information admitted or proven. However, the court held that the record reflected that defendant had abandoned any objection to the trial court's consideration of facts in the affidavit by stipulating to such facts. Reviewing the record, the court found that subsequent to a beating of the victim that defendant had been involved in, defendant threatened to beat the victim again, causing the victim to jump from defendant's vehicle, where defendant abandoned him to die. Under such facts, the court held that the trial court properly relied on the aggravating factors of deliberate cruelty and the victim's vulnerability in justifying the exceptional sentence.


OUTCOME: Criminal defendant minor's sentence of 60 months for his convictions of manslaughter and unlawful imprisonment was affirmed, as the sentence was imposed after consideration of relevant aggravating factors.

State v. Johnstone


No. 22232-9-II, Consolidated with No. 22244-2-II, No. 22245-1-II, No. 22246-9-II, No. 22281-7-II, No. 22299-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


96 Wn. App. 839; 982 P.2d 119; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1404



July 30, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington), which convicted them of intentional interference with owner's control, in violation of Wash. Rev. Stat. § 9.05.070.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed defendants' convictions for intentional interference with owner's control, in violation of Wash. Rev. Stat. § 9.05.070, and dismissed the charges against them without prejudice. Because defendants raised a challenge to the information charging them with the crime before their trial began, the court strictly construed the information and concluded that it did not contain all the essential elements of the crime necessary to notify defendants of the nature of the accusations against them. Using inartful and vague language, the information merely cited to the statute and named the offense. However, the information did not express the elements essential to establish the very illegality of the behavior as required for a conviction under the statute, including the specified enterprise that defendants interfered with and the fact that such enterprise was one wherein persons were employed for a wage. Therefore, defendants' convictions on the insufficient information could not stand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for intentional interference with owner's control and dismissed the charges against them because the information charging them with the crime failed to set forth the essential elements of the crimes.

Samis Land Co. v. City of Soap Lake


No. 17258-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


96 Wn. App. 819; 980 P.2d 805; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1389



July 27, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals August 12, 1999.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Amending Opinion August 12, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Wn. App. LEXIS 1504.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs petitioned for discretionary review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Grant County (Washington), denying plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment in a case wherein plaintiffs challenged the validity of a fee assessed by defendant municipality.


OVERVIEW: Defendant municipality adopted an ordinance which imposed a standby charge on vacant, unimproved land that abutted city water and sewer lines. Plaintiffs were owners of such property, and as such were assessed this charge. Upon plaintiffs' challenge of the ordinance as an invalid non-uniform tax, the court found it was not a valid regulatory fee as defined under the court's three-prong test. The ordinance made no reference to the type of service or benefits the paying landowner could expect to receive in exchange for payment of the standby charge. The money collected was not allocated only for authorized regulatory purposes. Instead, the types of costs supported appeared to be public benefits that cost money. Also, there was no direct relationship between the fee charged and the service received by or the burden produced by the ratepayer. Therefore, the standby fee appeared to be more of a tax than a regulatory fee. The trial court abused its discretion when it denied plaintiff's summary judgment motion, and the case was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: Plaintiffs landowners' challenge to validity of a fee assessed by defendant municipality was reversed and remanded, where the fee appeared to be an invalid non-uniform tax. There was no service or benefit to plaintiffs as a result of paying the fee, the money was not allocated for regulatory purposes, nor was there any relationship between the fee charged and the service received by or the burden produced by plaintiffs.

Rustlewood Ass'n v. Mason County


No. 22560-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


96 Wn. App. 788; 981 P.2d 7; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1365



July 23, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion Substituted on Denial of County's Motion for Reconsideration and Grant of Rustlewood's Motion for Reconsideration for Withdrawn Opinion of January 11, 1999, Previously Reported at: 969 P.2d 535; 969 P.2d 535, 1999 Wn. App. LEXIS 40 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Grays Harbor County (Washington), which entered a summary judgment in favor of appellee, and appellee sought a reconsideration of the trial court's denial of attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: This suit arose from a resolution enacted by appellant district to remedy what it perceived was an inequity in the manner in which charges were levied to finance a county-wide sewer and water system. Appellee district was granted a summary judgment on the grounds the law governing an account stated precluded appellant from making claims relating to sewer and water bills paid long ago, as was done by its Resolution. The court disagreed with the trial court's ruling that the contract doctrine of account stated was applicable, but agreed with the result and affirmed on an alternate ground. The court reasoned that by statute, the rates for the system maintenance had to be the same for the same class of customers. The court found that the county placed appellees in the same class and charged them the same rate, and could not have charged appellees what was in essence a higher rate than it charged others while they were in the same rate class. The court affirmed the decision denying appellees attorney fees under the common fund theory and 42 U.S.C.S. §19831, and found that fees were not available where appellees were resisting a legislative action that benefited a class of citizens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee upon a finding that the resolution enacted by appellant violated a statute governing the rates that a county could charge for the maintenance of the utility at issue. The court denied appellee's request for attorney fees because the requirements for recovery under the common fund theory or 42 U.S.C.S. § 19831 were not met.

Sintra, Inc. v. City of Seattle

OVERVIEW: Appellants, developer and various property owners, were sued by respondents, city and other property owners, in an action to enforce a housing preservation ordinance. The state supreme court reversed a judgment entered in favor of respondents and, after a trial, the jury rendered a verdict for appellants on an inverse condemnation claim. OUTCOME: Revised judgment of the trial court denying an award of postjudgment interest was remanded for correction because appellants were entitled to postjudgment interest on the costs of its award for the period of time that the award was on appeal and remained unpaid.

State v. Spencer


No. 22751-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1304



July 16, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied January 5, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wash. LEXIS 60.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 97-1-02168-7. Date filed: 12/10/1997. Judge signing: Hon. Thomas J. Felnagle.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions in the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) for first-degree murder by extreme indifference to human life and first-degree assault.


OVERVIEW: During an altercation, appellant fired a gun at four people and shot and killed one of them. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder by extreme indifference to human life and first-degree assault. Appellant challenged his conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed. The first-degree murder statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.030(1)(b), was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant, who should have known that firing his gun at the four people created a grave risk of death. As appellant did not object to the jury instruction he challenged on appeal, it was necessary for him to show that the instruction contained an error that violated his constitutional right. As the error alleged involved the definition of an element of first-degree murder, it did not involve a constitutional right. Also, two other instructions set forth all of the elements of the crime. As first-degree murder did not involve the same elements as first-degree assault, there was no double jeopardy violation. The crimes charged were against multiple victims and did not merge. As the two offenses did not involve the same criminal conduct, the trial court did not err by imposing consecutive sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant of first-degree murder by extreme indifference to human life and first-degree assault. The first-degree murder statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant; the jury instructions, taken as a whole, accurately defined "extreme indifference to human life"; appellant's convictions did not violate double jeopardy; and consecutive sentences were properly imposed.

Girton v. City of Seattle

State v. Partowkia


NO. 39060-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1228
