State v. Wilson


No. 42046-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


96 Wn. App. 382; 980 P.2d 244; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1237



July 6, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied January 5, 2000, Reported at: 139 Wn.2d 1018, 994 P.2d 846, 2000 Wash. LEXIS 25.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) imposing on him an exceptional sentence after he pleaded guilty to communicating with a minor for an immoral purpose, second degree assault, and failing to register as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to communicating with a minor for an immoral purpose, second degree assault, and failing to register as a sex offender after he engaged in two separate incidents of random attempted abductions of women within moments of each other and twice failed to register as a sex offender. The sentencing court imposed an exceptional sentence. On review of the sentence, the court affirmed. The evidence was sufficient to persuade a fair-minded person that the second victim's injuries were substantially greater than typical for a second degree assault case. If the sentencing court had not considered appellant's prior unscored misdemeanor of failing to register as a sex offender, the result would have been a presumptive range sentence that was too lenient. The phrase "seriousness of the victim's injuries," as an aggravating factor leading to an exceptional sentence, was not unconstitutionally vague, did not infringe upon appellant's right to appeal his exceptional sentence, and did not violate appellant's right to equal protection and due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's exceptional sentence because the sentencing court's reasons for imposing the exceptional sentence were legally adequate and supported by the record and because the statutes authorizing exceptional sentences were not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant.

 

1252 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Major Prods. Co. v. N.W. Harvest


No. 42557-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


96 Wn. App. 405; 979 P.2d 905; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1247; 42 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 755



July 6, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied November 2, 1999, Reported at: 139 Wn.2d 1007, 989 P.2d 1141, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 746.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditor challenged the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington) that held that respondent Chief Executive Officer was not personally liable for a debt.


OVERVIEW: Respondent debtor fell behind on its trade account with appellant creditor. Appellant sent a note for the debt to respondent debtor and respondent Chief Executive Officer (CEO) signed the note, attached a Post-It brand fax transmittal memo indicating that the note came from him, and sent the note via facsimile. The note went unpaid, and appellant sued both respondent CEO and respondent debtor. The trial court found that the writing on the Post-It, along with the signature, identified respondent debtor as the principal on the note. It held that respondent CEO was not personally liable for the debt because he signed the note as an agent for respondent debtor. On appeal, the court concluded that the writing on a Post-It brand fax transmittal memo was independent of the underlying document. Respondent CEO bore the burden of rebutting a presumption of personal liability. Because he did not provide evidence that rebutted that presumption, he was personally liable on the note and the trial court's judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that held that respondent Chief Executive Officer was not personally liable on a debt to appellant creditor was reversed because respondent failed to present extrinsic evidence to rebut a presumption of personal liability.

Sackett v. Santilli


No. 44892-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


101 Wn. App. 128; 5 P.3d 11; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 2227



July 6, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted January 9, 2001, Reported at: 142 Wn.2d 1016, 16 P.3d 1264, 2001 Wn. LEXIS 17.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 98-2-03749-1 SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: July 2, 1999. Superior Court Judge Signing: Hon. Jim Bates.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment from the Superior Court County: King (Washington) that his failure to timely file a jury demand was a waiver pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 38.


OVERVIEW: Respondent sued appellant for negligence in a motor vehicle accident. Appellant failed to timely file a jury demand. Construing Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 38, the trial court found that appellant waived trial by jury and, in its discretion, denied his later motions for jury trial and a new trial. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying the motion for jury trial and the motion for a new trial because an implied waiver, as defined in Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 38, constituted a valid consent to waiver of a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that appellant's failure to timely file a jury demand constituted a waiver. Appellant's implied waiver constituted a valid consent to waive his right to a jury trial.

State v. Bright


No. 22071-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1218



July 2, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 96 Wn. App. 1024.


PRIOR HISTORY: Docket No: 94-2-00391-1. Date filed: 04/28/1997. Judge signing: Hon. Toni A. Sheldon.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a Superior Court (Washington) decision that reversed respondent's multiple district court convictions of cruelty to animals.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state charged respondent with 18 counts of animal cruelty under former Wash. Rev. Code § 16.52.070 after a veterinarian and animal control officer visited her kennel. Using the veterinarian's revised report, the state obtained a search warrant of the kennel. This led to the removal of 59 dogs and 4 cats, a number of which exhibited health and hygiene problems. Respondent moved to suppress the evidence obtained from the search. The district court denied the motion and convicted her on all 18 counts. She then appealed to the superior court. The superior court reversed the convictions, finding former § 16.52.070 to be unconstitutionally vague because of its lack of sufficient standards to prevent arbitrary enforcement. The state appealed. On appeal, the court concluded that the statute's failure to describe the proscribed conduct with sufficient particularity invited law enforcement to exercise an inordinate amount of discretion. The court held that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that the district court convicted respondent without fair, solid, and substantial cause. The superior court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court that reversed respondent's convictions for cruelty to animals was affirmed because the statute was unconstitutionally vague and the district court convicted respondent without fair, solid, and substantial cause.

City of Spokane v. Carlson


No. 16739-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


96 Wn. App. 279; 979 P.2d 880; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1214



July 1, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a decision from the Superior Court (Washington) convicting him of failing to stop at the scene of an accident to exchange information as required under Spokane, Wash. Municipal Code § 16.52.020(2).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner driver struck the rear end of another vehicle, pulled along the driver's side, waved, failed to indicate he was going to stop, and kept going. He allegedly stopped several blocks away and then returned to find the motorist he struck. Petitioner was charged with violating Spokane, Wash. Municipal Code § 16.52.020(2), which required him to stop at the scene of the accident and provide information. Petitioner challenged his conviction, claiming that it was unconstitutionally vague. In affirming the decision, the court ruled that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as petitioner knew he was required to stop. It also held that the statute imposed the burden of exchanging information on the motorist who caused the collision. Since petitioner knew he had been involved in the accident and failed to stop near the accident scene, he was guilty of violating the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction as it found that petitioner knew he had an accident and that he was required to stop at or close to the scene of the accident and exchange information and that he had failed to do so.

State v. Frazier


NO. 39781-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1210



June 28, 1999, Filed

DISPOSITION: Frazier's sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Superior Court of King County (Washington) that convicted him of second degree robbery and sentenced him to life in prison without early release under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, wearing a dark stocking cap and sunglasses, approached a teller at a bank, with a note that read, "Robbery! Big Bills First!" The teller, thinking that appellant was reaching for a gun, gave him money from her till. Appellant approached another teller and demanded money. The second teller, who also thought that appellant was reaching for a weapon, also gave him money. Appellant was arrested carrying the money in a plastic bag. No weapon was recovered. Appellant was convicted of second degree robbery and was sentenced to prison without the possibility of early release under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA). Appellant sought review of the judgment contending that it was error to count his non-Washington robbery convictions as "strikes" under the POAA. The court concluded that appellant's non-Washington robbery convictions were comparable to Washington's first or second degree robbery convictions, which were "most serious offenses" for sentencing purposes. Thus, the court affirmed the sentencing court's calculation of appellant's offender score.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's sentence of life in prison without early release because appellant's non-Washington robbery convictions were comparable to Washington's first or second degree robbery convictions, which were "most serious offenses" for sentencing purposes.

 

1258 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Deja Vu, Inc. v. City of Federal Way


No. 41818-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


96 Wn. App. 255; 979 P.2d 464; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1161



June 28, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult entertainment business challenged an order of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which granted appellee city summary judgment on appellant's suit to declare a city ordinance unconstitutional. Appellee contested the denial of its motion for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city's ordinance required erotic dancers in adult cabarets to stay at least four feet away from patrons. In 1996, appellant adult entertainment business sued appellee in federal court and challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance. The federal court ruled the ordinance was constitutional and granted appellee summary judgment. In 1997, the Washington Supreme Court affirmed the constitutionality of a similar ordinance. Later that year, appellant sued appellee in state court, challenging the constitutionality of the ordinance. The trial court granted appellee summary judgment but denied attorney fees. The appellate affirmed dismissal but reversed and remanded for an award of attorney fees. Principles of collateral estoppel and res judicata precluded litigation of the present suit. The Washington Supreme Court already ruled that a four-foot limit was constitutional. Also, appellant's present suit arose from the same nucleus of facts and involved the same parties as its suit in federal court. Appellee was entitled to recover attorney fees because the suit was frivolous.


OUTCOME: The order granting appellee city summary judgment was affirmed. Earlier decisions involving the same ordinance and parties clearly precluded the challenge to appellee's ordinance by appellant adult entertainment business. The order denying appellee attorney fees was reversed and remanded. Appellee was entitled to attorney fees for having to defend a frivolous suit at trial and on appeal.

Duwamish Valley Neighborhood Preservation Coalition v. Central Puget Sound Growth Mgmt. Hearings Bd.


No. 41523-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1135



June 21, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant coalition sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which affirmed respondent board's finding that respondent county had complied with a remand order requiring it to provide a reasonable opportunity for public participation on the change of land use designation of certain property, among other things. Appellant also requested attorney fees against respondent board under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.84.350.

The lower court affirmed respondent board's finding that respondent county had complied with its remand order requiring reasonable public participation. Appellant's request for attorney fees was denied because respondent board was acting as an adjudicative body and was a nominal party to this proceeding.

 

1260 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


No. 17116-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


95 Wn. App. 952; 977 P.2d 1242; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1046



June 10, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted January 5, 2000, Reported at: 139 Wn.2d 1015, 994 P.2d 845, 2000 Wash. LEXIS 20.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's prosecution from the Superior Court of Walla Walla County (Washington) for prison misbehavior pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94.070, was dismissed because the statute unconstitutionally delegated to the Department of Corrections the power to define a serious infraction, an element of the crime. The state appealed. Defendant cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an inmate with no time credits, was charged with persistent prison misbehavior after refusing to stand for a search. The trial court dismissed the charges, solely on the ground that the legislature had improperly delegated its authority under Wash. Const. art. II, § 1. On appeal, defendant argued that the delegation lacked adequate procedural safeguards. The court held that the legislature provided standards, which in general terms stated what was to be done and the administrative body that was to do it. The necessary procedural safeguards, however, were missing. Considering the four suggested safeguards as a whole, the court concluded that they did not sufficiently address the problem of delegating to the Department of Corrections (DOC) the authority to define a crime without legislative oversight or safeguard against prior loss of liberty. The suggested safeguards were inadequate to control and guard against arbitrary administrative actions or abuses of discretion prior to loss of liberty by criminal conviction. Consequently, Wash. Rev. Code 9.94.070 constituted an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority to the DOC.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conclusion that the legislature unconstitutionally delegated the authority to the Department of Corrections to define serious infractions. Although the legislature provided general terms to define what was to be done by the administrative body, the procedural safeguards were inadequate because they did not adequately control or guard against arbitrary administrative action or abuse of discretion.

State v. Burns


No. 22375-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1024



June 3, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clallam County. Docket No: 97-1-00070-9. Date filed: 08/25/1997. Judge signing: Hon. Kenneth D. Williams.



DISPOSITION: Convictions are affirmed, but monetary fine accompanying count I is stricken.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by the Superior Court of Clallam County (Washington) on misdemeanor charges of hunting without a license and hunting while a license was revoked, as well as the gross misdemeanor of harassment. Appellant challenged his convictions on numerous evidentiary, statutory interpretation, and constitutional grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with hunting without a license and hunting while a license was revoked, as well as the gross misdemeanor of harassment, after he and a friend were confronted on private property by a person working there. The employee advised the men that hunting with dogs was illegal, and the defendant's friend responded, generally admitting that they were hunting raccoons. At trial, the admissions made by the friend were introduced as "adoptive admissions" and were held not to be hearsay. Defendant was convicted of the charges. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, finding no error in the trial court proceedings, but vacated the imposition of a fine as to the charge of hunting without a license, on grounds this charge was merged into the charge of hunting after forfeiture of license. The court found that facts were sufficient to established the corpus delicti of hunting and that the adoptive admission was properly admitted. The court held that the testimony of the witness was introduced for the purpose of impeachment as important facts in appellee's case were established by the witness, and that there was substantial evidence to support the convictions.


OUTCOME: Finding no error with the trial court proceedings, the court affirmed appellant's conviction on misdemeanor charges of hunting without a license and hunting while a license was revoked, as well as the gross misdemeanor of harassment. However the court struck and reversed the monetary fine accompanying one count because it found that two counts were merged.

State v. Moten


No. 42398-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


95 Wn. App. 927; 976 P.2d 1286; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 991



June 1, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted appellant, based on a guilty plea, of a violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.28.030 and sentenced him to 32 months in prison.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction, based on a guilty plea, for violating the state's controlled substance law, appellant claimed he was sentenced under the wrong statute and that his sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The court first held that the judgment form merely contained a scrivener's error concerning the statutes under which appellant was convicted and sentenced. The court ordered the error corrected and held that it was not prejudicial to appellant. The court then noted that the sentence appellant received was less than the recommended sentence that he agreed upon in the plea bargain he accepted. Following analogous case law, the court held that appellant's plea agreement to a sentence that was less than the maximum recommended under state guidelines precluded his disproportionality challenge. As a result, the court upheld the sentence.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction and sentence for violating the state's controlled substances statute was affirmed because appellant had waived his challenge to the sentence. However, the case was remanded to correct a scrivener's error on the judgment form.

State v. Doran


No. 44093-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 983



June 1, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 95 Wn. App. 1068.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Whatcom County. Docket No: 98-1-00800-1. Date filed: 10/08/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Michael F. Moynihan.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court of Whatcom County (Washington), which convicted him of telephone harassment and for violating a no-contact order. Specifically, defendant challenged that part of the order that required him to leave the county of his residence after his release from jail.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for telephone harassment and for violating a no-contact order that his sister had obtained while fearing for her safety. Defendant was ordered to leave the county after his release from jail. Defendant did not leave the county and was later arrested for violating the conditions of his sentence. The trial judge affirmed the geographic restriction, stating that the victim's right to security prevailed over defendant's right to live where he desired. Defendant filed an emergency motion, requesting an order for immediate release and stay of the geographical restriction pending further proceedings; defendant argued the restriction violated his constitutional right to travel. On review, the court found that the state had a compelling interest in protecting the victim from defendant's harassment that justified a narrowly tailored limitation on the offender's right to travel. However, the sentencing court's order imposing a geographical restriction on an entire county was also unnecessarily broad because the record did not indicate that the victim frequented so much of the county to justify a county-wide ban. The case was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: An order requiring defendant to leave the county of his residence after his release from jail, as part of his sentence for telephone harassment and for violating a no-contact order, was reversed. The court acknowledged that the state had a compelling interest in protecting the victim from defendant's harassment, but that such a geographical restriction on defendant's right to travel within an entire county was unnecessarily broad.

In re Det. of Gallegos


No. 14903-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SIX

NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 95 Wn. App. 1055.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Chelan County. Docket No: 95-2-00013-9. Date filed: 04/19/1995. Judge signing: Hon. Ted W. Small Jr.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Chelan County (Washington) finding him in contempt of court for refusing to participate in a court-ordered mental health evaluation to determine whether he was a sexually violent predator, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09. Appellant contended that he was denied effective assistance of counsel when his attorney was not allowed to participate in the evaluation process.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of three violent rapes committed within a two-year time span. Shortly before he was scheduled to be released from prison, the state filed a petition for civil commitment, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09, seeking a determination that appellant was a sexually violent predator. After a probable cause hearing, appellant was detained and ordered to undergo a mental health evaluation to determine whether he was a sexually violent predator. Appellant challenged a trial court judgment finding him in contempt of court for refusing to participate in the court-ordered evaluation. Appellant contended that he was denied effective assistance of counsel when his attorney was not allowed to participate in the evaluation process. The appeals court affirmed the trial court decision. The court ruled that appellant had the right to have his attorney observe, but not participate in, the standardized psychological testing. The court added that while appellant was entitled to counsel at all stages of the proceedings, that did not include assistance with answering the questions in the psychological testing, because that would undermine the validity of the test.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court decision because appellant's right to counsel at all stages of the proceedings did not include assistance with answering the questions in the psychological testing. The court also ruled that the sexually violent predator act was a civil proceeding and involuntary confinement pursuant to the act was not punitive or further charges.

Dang v. Ehredt


No. 42236-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


95 Wn. App. 670; 977 P.2d 29; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 890



May 17, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Order Denying Motion for Reconsideration June 28, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Wn. App. LEXIS 1212.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order from the Superior Court of King County (Washington) granting summary judgment to defendants in an action for false arrest, false imprisonment, deprivation of civil rights, and negligence.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff wife was arrested by defendant police officers when she tried to cash her paycheck at defendant bank because defendant bank believed her check was a counterfeit. After it had been determined that the check was valid, plaintiff wife and plaintiff husband brought suit for false arrest, false imprisonment, deprivation of civil rights, and negligence against defendants, the city, police department, police officers, and bank. The trial court granted summary judgment for defendants, and the court affirmed the summary judgment order. The court declined to hear issues raised for the first time in plaintiffs' appellate brief. Defendant police officers were entitled to qualified immunity from liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and from liability for false arrest because they acted reasonably under settled law under the circumstances. Defendant bank was protected by the immunity afforded by Wash. Rev. Code § 4.24.510 from liability for negligence because defendant bank merely communicated information to defendant police officers. Defendant bank did not falsely imprison plaintiff wife because it did not deprive her of liberty of movement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment order because defendant police officers were entitled to qualified immunity from liability, and defendant bank was statutorily entitled to immunity because defendant bank merely communicated its version of the facts to defendant police officers and asked the officers for assistance.

 

1268 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. L.K.


No. 42824-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


95 Wn. App. 686; 977 P.2d 39; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 891



May 17, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected May 17, 1999.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the King County Superior Court (Washington) denying her motion to suppress narcotics discovered by the police when they stopped and frisked her.


OVERVIEW: Police officers saw defendant, who appeared to be a youth at risk, on a street corner on a school night with older companions who had been prosecuted for drug offenses. After the officers physically stopped defendant, she seemed nervous and refused to keep her hands in view; the officers frisked her, discovering illegal drugs. Defendant moved to suppress the narcotics on the basis they were illegally seized. Defendant's motion was denied, and she appealed. The court affirmed denial of the motion. The court determined the officers seized defendant when they took hold of her arm to stop her. Applying a balancing test, the court held defendant's interest in being free of police interference was outweighed by the officers' legitimate attempt to carry out their community caretaking function; defendant initially refused to let officers find out if she was in danger, and her seizure was thus justified. There was no proof defendant's stop was a pretext for an illegal search. The officers properly frisked defendant based on a reasonable belief she was harboring a weapon; the scope of the frisk was valid. The narcotics, simultaneously in plain view during the frisk, were properly seized.


OUTCOME: Order denying defendant's motion to suppress narcotics was affirmed because defendant was properly stopped by police officers who were carrying out their function as community caretakers; there was no proof the stop was a pretext for an illegal search. Further, the frisk which uncovered the narcotics was proper because it was based on the officers' reasonable belief defendant had a weapon.

 

1269 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carter


No. 21394-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 871



May 14, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied December 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Wash. LEXIS 852. Reported in Table Case Format at: 95 Wn. App. 1042.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 96-1-00452-7. Date filed: 12/02/1996. Judge signing: Hon. Leonard W. Costello.



DISPOSITION: Vacated in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington) that convicted appellant of first and second degree murder, under Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.32.030(1)(c), 9A.08.020, and 9A.32.050(b). Appellant was convicted as a persistent offender, under § 9.94A.120(4), and was sentenced to life in prison without a possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Upon a jury verdict, appellant was convicted of first and second degree murder, under Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.32.030(1)(c), 9A.08.020, and 9A.32.050(b). Appellant was convicted under the persistent offender statute, § 9.94A.120(4), and was sentenced to life in prison with no possibility of parole. The appellate court vacated the second degree murder conviction, under § 10.43.020, as conceded by respondent state. However, the judgment was otherwise affirmed. The appellate court held that appellant failed to preserve an issue for review. Furthermore, it was not an abuse of discretion for the trial court to allow evidence of appellant's prior bad act because it was introduced to rebut appellant's assertions. Even if the admission was in error, it was harmless error because substantial evidence supported the conviction. Statements of appellant's inmate were not admitted in error because there was no evidence that the inmate was a state agent. Because the evidence supported the first degree murder conviction, appellant suffered no injustice on double jeopardy grounds. Finally, the appellate court held that, based on precedent, § 9.94A.120(4) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Appellant's second degree murder conviction was vacated because, as conceded by respondent state, double jeopardy prohibited conviction for different degrees of a crime involving the same incident and victim. The conviction and sentence for first degree murder was affirmed because substantial evidence supported the conviction, and admission of an inmate's statement was not erroneous because there was no evidence the inmate was a state agent.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), committing him to a secure facility following a finding that he was a sexually violent predator pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of a commitment order entered following a finding that he was a sexually violent predator pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09. State v. Cloud

NOTICE:  PUBLISHED IN PART

Rev Code § 9.94A.120(4).


OVERVIEW: Appellant student shot and killed a teacher who had sexually abused him for many years. A jury convicted appellant of first degree murder. Appellant moved to set aside the verdict for ineffective assistance of counsel. The trial court denied the motion after holding a hearing in which it allowed appellant's counsel to intervene as a third party. Even though appellant was a first time offender, the trial court sentenced him under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act, Wash. Rev Code § 9.94A.120(4). Appellant sought review. The court reversed and remanded for a new hearing on appellant's motion for a new trial because the trial court erred in allowing appellant's former counsel to intervene. The court also remanded for imposition of a new sentence allowing appellant to earn early release time because the part of § 9.94A.120(4) which applied to first time offenders unconstitutionally exceeded the scope of the initiative's ballot title.


OUTCOME: Denial of appellant student's motion for new trial was reversed and remanded for new hearing because the trial court erred in allowing appellant's former counsel to intervene. Appellant's sentence under the persistent offender statute was remanded because the statute could not apply to first time offenders.

OVERVIEW: Appellant assaulted two women in two separate incidents. In the second incident, he used a firearm to threaten the woman. The court, however, vacated the exceptional sentence for appellant's firearm offense because it was an element of his assault conviction.


OUTCOME: Appellant's exceptional sentence for his firearm offense was vacated because it was an element of his assault conviction. His sentences for the assaults were affirmed because the sentencing guidelines were not unconstitutionally vague.

Children's Hosp. v. Dep't of Health


No. 23480-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


95 Wn. App. 858; 975 P.2d 567; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 791



April 30, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review Denied January 6, 2000, Reported at: 139 Wn.2d 1021, 994 P.2d 847, 2000 Wash. LEXIS 8.
Modified by, Reconsideration denied by Children's Hosp. & Med. Ctr. v. Washington State Dep't of Health, 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1445 (Wash. Ct. App., Aug. 6, 1999)
Review denied by Children's Hosp. & Med. Ctr. v. Department of Health, 139 Wn.2d 1021, 994 P.2d 847, 2000 Wash. LEXIS 8 (2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which found that plaintiff was not entitled to relief in its suit challenging the Washington State Department of Health's determination that a hospital could perform pediatric open heart surgeries without a Certificate of Need review.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a children's hospital, filed a petition for judicial review, challenging the Washington State Department of Health's determination that another hospital could perform pediatric open heart surgeries without a Certificate of Need (CN) review. The court found plaintiff was not entitled to relief under Wash. Rev. Code § 34.05.570(4), which allows relief for performance by an agency action, only if the action was unconstitutional, outside the statutory authority of the agency or the authority conferred by a provision of law, or arbitrary or capricious, or taken by people not properly constituted as agency officials lawfully entitled to such action. The court dismissed the hospital's petition for judicial review. Plaintiff appealed. The court reversed, finding that pediatric open heart surgery was a specialized inpatient pediatric service that required CN review, that pediatric open heart surgery was a tertiary health service that was new to the hospital, and required CN review, and the Department's determination to the contrary was arbitrary and capricious. Thus, before the hospital could perform pediatric open heart surgery, the Department must first conduct CN review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the determination that plaintiff was not entitled to relief, finding that the hospital in question could perform pediatric open heart surgery, only if the Department of Health first conducted a Certificate of Need review.

State v. Huereca


NOS. 39755-9-I, 39852-1-I Consolidated Cases


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 769



April 26, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-1-06553-4. Date filed: 12/03/1996. Judge signing: Hon. Faith Ireland.



DISPOSITION: Verdicts and sentences for both defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), entering judgment of conviction of kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, attempted robbery in the first degree, and rape in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Appellants attacked four people, hijacked their car, took their property, and sexually assaulted a victim. The trial court convicted appellants of kidnapping, robbery, attempted robbery, and rape. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court did not err in refusing to sever the trial because appellants' defenses were not mutually antagonistic, and appellants did not show resulting prejudice. The admission of prior crimes into evidence was not in error, as the crimes were admissible under Wash. R. Evid. 404(b) as proof of plan, motive, and identity. The warrantless search of an appellant's apartment was legal as a resident with common authority over the apartment consented. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that the charges for the kidnapping and robbery were not part of the same criminal conduct, as they occurred in different locations. The firearm enhancements were proper although the jury specially found that the defendants were armed with a deadly weapon, not with a firearm. One appellant received a fair trial as the prosecutor's statement that appellant had not gone to the police after the crimes was improper but amounted to harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction; the trial court did nor err in denying motions for severance, admitting prior crimes as evidence of plan and motive, finding that the kidnapping and rape charges did not comprise the same criminal conduct, or imposing firearm enhancements; the warrantless search was legal because the police had consent to search.

State v. Robinson


No. 22501-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 750



April 23, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 97-1-00325-3. Date filed: 10/06/1997. Judge signing: Hon. John F. Nichols.



DISPOSITION: Robinson's conviction affirmed but his sentence as persistent offender reversed, and remanded for resentencing, with prior convictions being counted in criminal history if appropriate.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington) convicting him of first degree burglary and robbery and sentencing him as a persistent offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced as a persistent offender after he was convicted of burglary and robbery. Defendant claimed his two prior offenses, in another state, could not be used as the elements were different under the two state laws. Since aggravated battery was the most serious offense defendant was convicted of in the other state, and was comparable to the state's crime of second degree assault, this conviction could be used. However, his prior conviction for robbery had a different intent standard and could not be used. Defendant argued his out of state conviction for battery was unconstitutional. The court ruled the state only needed to prove the conviction, not the validity of the conviction. Thus, defendant had to be resentenced based on the one prior offense. In the challenge to defendant's conviction, the court found that due process could not be presumed based upon his attorney's compensation. Defendant was required to demonstrate prejudice to his rights. It also found no error in the photo identification by the victim and affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of both burglary and robbery, finding no errors in the identification or ineffective counsel. However, he had to be resentenced as one of the predicate offenses could not be counted against him.

State v. McCready


No. 16540-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 749



April 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

Defendant filed a cross-appeal alleging ineffective assistance of counsel and unconstitutional vagueness of the sentence enhancement statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.310(3)(e).

State v. Miller


No. 38560-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 689



April 19, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied January 5, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Wash. LEXIS 42.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 98 Wn. App. 1003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-1-06188-1. Date filed: 04/08/1996. Judge signing: Hon. Laura Inveen.



DISPOSITION: Miller's conviction for felony stalking affirmed; his conviction for felony harassment reversed; and case remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision from Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of felony stalking and felony harassment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant threatened to kill the victim in a way which made her believe that he would carry out his threat; however, he made no specific threats to commit bodily harm in the future. Appellant was convicted of both felony stalking and felony harassment and appealed the convictions, arguing that there was insufficient evidence to convict him of felony stalking, that there were no specific threats to commit bodily harm in the future to support the conviction for felony harassment, and that the words used in the phone calls were constitutionally protected speech. The court disagreed with the felony stalking argument noting that, not only did an insufficiency argument admit the truth of the prosecution's evidence, but the fact that appellant contacted the victim after being served with a no-contact order was prima facie evidence of felony stalking. The court held also that the words spoken during the phone calls were not constitutionally protected speech because they were "fighting words." The court did, however, reverse on the felony harassment charge agreeing with appellant that there was no evidence of a future threat of bodily harm.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction on felony stalking was affirmed because the evidence was sufficient and the words spoken during the phone calls were "fighting words" and not constitutionally protected speech. The harassment conviction was reversed because there were no future threats made.

State v. Rosul


No. 41124-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


95 Wn. App. 175; 974 P.2d 916; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 693



April 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Denying Appellant's Motion for Reconsideration June 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1043.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington) that convicted him, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.070, of one count of possession of a depiction of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct. Appellant asserted that the trial court erroneously instructed the jury and that the trial court's erroneous jury instructions rendered § 9.68A.070 unconstitutionally vague and violative of due process.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction of one count of possession of a depiction of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct, arguing that the trial court erred by failing to instruct the jury that knowledge of the minor status of the individual depicted was an essential element of the offense, by basing his conviction on a statute which did not proscribe possession of digitized images of child pornography, and by instructing the jury that visual or printed matter included material that could be viewed either with the human eye or with the aid of devices which transform it so that it could be viewed. Appellant also claimed that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.070 was overbroad and violative of due process. On appeal, the court affirmed. Knowledge of the age of the persons depicted in sexually explicit material was not an essential element of § 9.68A.070. Under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.011(2), the computerized pornographic images possessed by appellant fell within the proscriptions of § 9.68A.070. It was not inappropriate for the trial court to clarify for the jury the definition of visual or printed matter as used in § 9.68A.070.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of one count of possession of a depiction of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct. Knowledge of the minor status of the person depicted was not an element of the offense, the applicable statute was not overbroad or violative of due process, and the trial court appropriately clarified the statutory language in its instruction to the jury.

Kanna v. Benton County


No. 17270-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 659



April 15, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Klickitat County. Docket No: 97-2-00070-5. Date filed: 02/12/1998. Judge signing: Hon. E. T. Reynolds.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Klickitat County (Washington), denying their application for a preliminary plat.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a group of homeowners, filed an application for a preliminary plat with the county board of commissioners (Board). The Board denied the application, and the trial court affirmed the decision. On appeal, appellants argued that the Board had no authority to deny the plat because of risks of pesticide migration from a neighboring orchard, that the Board's decision was not supported by substantial evidence, that the decision was an unconstitutional taking of private property for public use, and that the decision violated their right of substantive due process. The court ruled that the Board had authority under Wash. Rev. Code § 58.17.110, to consider whether the proposed plat was compatible with the lawful operation of the neighboring orchard. Further, the court held that the test of substantial evidence was whether evidence was sufficient to persuade a fair-minded person of the truth of the declared premise, and that the Board's findings were supported by substantial evidence. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that appellants' taking claim was not ripe under federal constitutional analysis, and that appellants could not raise a substantive due process claim.


OUTCOME: Judgment denying appellants' plat application was affirmed where the county board of commissioners had the authority to deny the plat and its decision was supported by substantial evidence. Appellants' claim that the decision was an unconstitutional taking of private property for public use was not ripe under federal constitutional analysis, and the claim that the decision violated appellants' substantive due process rights was without merit.

East Wind Express v. Airborne Freight


No. 23336-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


95 Wn. App. 98; 974 P.2d 369; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 620



April 9, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a prior holder of a cartage contract with appellee, a nationwide delivery service, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington), which granted summary judgment to appellee. The court found that appellant did not have a franchise relationship with appellee and, therefore, appellee could terminate its cartage contract at will.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee, a nationwide delivery service, in an action brought by appellant, prior holder of a cartage contract with appellee, based on an alleged violation of a state franchise act. The court held that appellant did not have a franchise relationship with appellee as defined in Wash. Rev. Code § 19.100.010(4) because appellant merely provided transportation services for appellee. Appellant did not offer, sell, or distribute transportation services to the customers who shipped goods with appellee. Accordingly, appellant was an independent contractor and was not entitled to the benefits of the Washington Franchise Investment Protection Act (FIPA), Wash. Rev. Code § 19.100.940. Appellee was entitled to terminate the cartage contract at will.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a grant of summary judgment to appellee because appellant was not entitled to the protections of a state franchise act, and, accordingly, appellee could terminate the party's cartage contract at will.

Rural Residents v. Kitsap County


No. 41281-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


95 Wn. App. 383; 974 P.2d 863; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 545



March 29, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a decision from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which invalidated the county commissioners' approval of appellants' plan for development of a 123-acre parcel of land as violative of the Growth Management Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70.


OVERVIEW: Approval of appellants' filed plan and planned unit development (PUD) application was invalidated by the trial court. The trial court improperly held that the PUD application did not vest to the zoning laws in effect when the application was filed, and this portion of its decision was reversed. However, the zoning laws to which the project did vest included the county's Interim Urban Growth Area. Consequently, the project was subject to the Growth Management Act's (GMA), Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70, prohibition against growth, urban in nature, outside an urban growth area. Because appellants did not show that their project could be compatible with the primary use of such land for the production of food, other agricultural products, or fiber, or the extraction of mineral resources, it was considered urban development. Approval of the project, therefore, violated the GMA because it allowed development, which was urban in nature, to occur outside the area designated for interim urban growth. Judgment reversing the commissioners' decision to approve the application was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment invalidating county commissioners' approval of appellants' planned unit development as violative of Growth Management Act was affirmed, where the development was urban in nature and was to continue in a geographic area outside of that statutorily designated for urban development. Finding that appellants did not have a vested right to have their application considered only under the zoning laws in effect when it was filed was reversed.

 

1283 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arroyo


No. 42115-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 566



March 29, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 94 Wn. App. 1054.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-1-08021-1. Date filed: 02/02/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Stephen G. Scott.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which issued a sentence enhancement under Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435(a) for delivery of heroin within 1000 feet of a school bus route stop. Defendant contended that the state violated his right to due process because the special verdict was based on his proximity to a school bus route stop.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals upheld a judgment issuing a sentence enhancement under Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435(a) for delivery of heroin within 1000 feet of a school bus route stop. Defendant contended that the school bus route stop enhancement was unconstitutional as applied to him because he did not have fair notice that his conduct was subject to an enhanced penalty. Defendant contended that the state failed to prove that he could have learned the location of the school bus route stop by any readily understandable or available means. The court noted that the focus of a court's inquiry was not the number of children served by a bus stop, but the daily appearance of a bus picking up school-aged children, which was sufficient to put drug dealers on notice of the possibility of a school bus stop. The court found that in addition to personal observation, defendant had other understandable and available means to determine the existence of a school bus stop at the location, such as contacting the school district for a map or list of school bus stops. The court concluded that the facts were sufficient to support the sentence enhancement.


OUTCOME: A judgment that issued a sentence enhancement to defendant for delivery of heroin within 1000 feet of a school bus route stop was affirmed because there were readily understandable and available means to determine the location of the school bus stop.

 

1284 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Stearns v. City of Gig Harbor


No. 22912-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 528



March 26, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1048.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 94 Wn. App. 1051.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 96-2-09000-5. Date filed: 06/06/1997. Judge signing: Hon. Karen L. Strombom.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants contested a ruling from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) that their building site plan did not meet zoning requirements, claiming that the requirements in effect at the time of filing differed from the ones used for approval purposes. Appellants argued for reversal under the Land Use Petition Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.


OVERVIEW: The court considered whether appellants had a vested right to have the site plan application evaluated on the basis of the city code as it existed when the application was made. Because the city code allowed a developer to fix a date by filing a building permit, filing the site plan application did not vest appellants' rights to have their application processed according to the code in effect at filing. Further, where appellants offered copies of World Wide Web pages as proof of the code in existence when they filed, the court held that the web pages did not shed light on the legislative intent of the city council. Rather, they showed, at best, staff interpretation of the code. These were not legislative facts of which the court could take judicial notice. Moreover, the court declined to take judicial notice where appellants failed to move under the Land Use Petition Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C, to supplement the administrative record with the web pages. Respondent city was entitled to reasonable attorney's fees in an amount to be set by a court commissioner.


OUTCOME: Where appellants filed a building site plan, not a building permit application, the doctrine of vested rights did not apply, and appellant did not lock in the city zoning requirements at the time of filing. Copies of World Wide Web pages were not subject to judicial notice where no motion to supplement the record was filed, and appellants' case was dismissed.

 

1285 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Gig Harbor Marina v. City of Gig Harbor


No. 22906-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


94 Wn. App. 789; 973 P.2d 1081; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 530



March 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review denied at 138 Wn.2d 1016 (1999).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) dismissing petitioners' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action seeking relief from respondent city's denial of petitioners' land use application under the Land Use Petition Act, Wash. Rev. Code 36.70C, as frivolous and awarding respondent attorney fees under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.84.370.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, whose land use application filed under the Land Use Petition Act, Wash. Rev. Code 36.70C, was denied by respondent city, challenged the trial court's dismissal of their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action as frivolous as well as the court's award of attorney fees to respondent. On appeal, the court held that under the equal protection analysis, Wash. Rev. Code § 4.84.370, which defined a party's liability for the attorney fees and costs of the opposing party on appeal of a local land use decision, was neutral both on its face and in its application to petitioners. Additionally, Wash. Rev. Code § 4.84.370 (1) did not prevent petitioners from having meaningful access to the courts under U.S. Const. amend. I, and (2) was not preempted by the attorney fee provisions of 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1988.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of petitioner's civil rights suit because respondent's denial of a land use application was proper under local ordinance and because a state statute requiring petitioners to pay respondent's appellate attorney fees was constitutional.

State v. Frank


No. 15808-0-III, No. 15818-7-III, No. 16185-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL NINE


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 520



March 23, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied November 3, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Wash. LEXIS 729.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 94 Wn. App. 1047.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Okanogan County. Docket No: 95-1-00206-2. Date filed: 05/10/1996. Judge signing: Hon. Kenneth L. Jorgensen.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Okanogan County (Washington), which convicted them, upon a jury verdict, of child molestation in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a married couple, were charged with child molestation in the first degree. They were tried together and represented by the same trial lawyer. The jury found both appellants guilty. On appeal, they argued for reversal on several grounds, including ineffective assistance of counsel, insufficient evidence, inadmissible hearsay, and prosecutorial misconduct. The court found that appellant counsel's joint representation posed no actual conflict of interest, which impinged their U.S. Const. amend. VI right to counsel. It was not enough to show a possibility of a conflict of interest; specific instances in the record were required. The court also held that there was no abuse of discretion with regard to the trial court's admission of child hearsay testimony. The trial court properly considered the nine Ryan factors of reliability, and a child's response to questions on sexual abuse fulfilled the spontaneity requirement of the analysis. The court further held that the prosecutor's closing arguments, wherein the prosecutor used the phrases "I think," "I don't think," or "I believe" when referring to the witnesses or evidence were not improper.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment convicting appellants of child molestation in the first degree was affirmed, where hearsay statements were admissible, trial counsel was effective, and prosecutorial comments given during closing arguments were not improper.

 

1287 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crawford


No. 21641-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 491



March 19, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] ULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 94 Wn. App. 1042.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clallam County. Docket No: 96-1-00166-9. Date filed: 01/17/1997 Judge signing: Hon. George L. Wood Jr.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contested a ruling from the Superior Court of Clallam County (Washington) denying her motion to suppress evidence of marijuana found pursuant to a search warrant. Appellant argued that the affidavit did not establish probable cause and that her motion to dismiss challenging Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.402(a)(6) for vagueness should have been granted.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the conviction, finding the affidavit information sufficient to allow a reasonable inference that there was marijuana inside one or more of the buildings searched pursuant to the warrant. Further, a person of ordinary intelligence would understand that Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.402(a)(6) prohibited a person from acting so as to take responsibility for the physical or financial upkeep of real property that was used for drug related purposes. Although there was sufficient evidence to establish appellant's knowledge of the drug use and business occurring on her property, there was minimal evidence that she was personally active in drug use or distribution. Yet no reasonable juror could become confused by the language of the jury instruction. Because the statutory language was sufficiently precise to give fair warning of prohibited conduct, and clear enough to provide ascertainable standards of guilt, the court rejected appellant's vagueness challenge and affirmed the lower court's orders.


OUTCOME: Because a reasonable person of ordinary intelligence could understand what conduct a drug house statute proscribed, and what the standard of guilt was, the statute was not overly vague, and the court affirmed the conviction.

State v. Smith


No. 22372-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 493



March 19, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 94 Wn. App. 1042.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 96-1-00449-7. Date filed: 07/16/1997. Judge signing: Hon. Jay B. Roof.



DISPOSITION: The conviction of second degree murder is vacated; the conviction of first degree murder and the sentence of life without parole as a persistent offender are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contested his conviction and sentence for first degree and second degree felony murder from the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), as well as the determination of persistent offender status based in part on an out of state robbery conviction.


OVERVIEW: The court vacated a second degree murder conviction because conviction on two counts for one murder violated double jeopardy protections. The court affirmed the conviction for first degree murder, finding no significant evidentiary errors. Appellant's classification as a persistent offender and sentence of life without parole were affirmed. It was not evident from the face of appellant's prior plea that he was unaware of the elements of the crime or the consequences of the plea. Accordingly, his conviction was not unconstitutional on its face. Further, the applicable definition of first degree robbery in the other state was comparable to the Washington definition where both required the taking of property from or in the presence of another person by force or fear of force while armed with a deadly weapon. Accordingly, the lower court did not err in holding that the conviction counted in determining appellant's persistent offender status. As he acknowledged that he had waived his right to allocution, appellant ratified his waiver, and it was valid. Where appellant did not make an offer of proof later at trial, the issue was waived, and could not be argued on appeal.


OUTCOME: Vacating the second degree murder conviction on double jeopardy grounds, the court affirmed the first degree murder conviction, classification as a persistent offender and the life sentence where appellant was aware of the crime's elements and consequences at the time of the prior plea and the applicable out of state conviction was properly counted for persistent offender purposes.

State v. Welch


No. 23056-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 460



March 12, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 94 Wn. App. 1038.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pacific County. Docket No: 98-1-00006-4. Date filed: 03/06/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Joel M. Penoyar.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a decision of the Superior Court of Pacific County (Washington), which convicted and sentenced appellant for assault in the third degree by criminal negligence under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.031(1)(f).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and sentenced for assault in the third degree by criminal negligence. Appellant contended that her procedural due process rights were violated because the common understanding of assault required intentional behavior. Appellant argued that the legislature could not redefine assault to include negligent assault, and that it was unconstitutional for appellant to be convicted under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.031(1)(f). The instant court stated that the statute specifically listed criminal negligence as one way that a person could commit assault. It was clear on the face of the statute that the culpable mental state for third-degree assault had been legislatively broadened. Further, the legislature's power to define crimes and prescribe punishment was virtually exclusive, nearly unlimited, and left practically no correlative power to do the same in the courts. Thus, appellant's conviction of negligent assault did not violate her constitutional rights. Further, the court held that appellant's actions were inconsistent of a person in the position of a live-in caretaker, and that appellant's actions warranted an exceptional sentence.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the conviction and sentence of appellant for assault in the third degree by criminal negligence, on grounds that it was clear on the face of the statute that the culpable mental state for third-degree assault had been legislatively broadened; that the legislature's power to define crimes and prescribe punishment was virtually exclusive; and that appellant's actions warranted an exceptional sentence.

Welfare of H.S.


No. 17264-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


94 Wn. App. 511; 973 P.2d 474; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 446



March 9, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied May 15, 2000, Reported at: 529 U.S. 1108, 120 S. Ct. 1960, 146 L. Ed. 2d 792, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3186. [As Amended by order of the Court of Appeals April 15, 1999.] Reported at: 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 753.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which granted the request of respondent agency to terminate their parental rights because they both suffered from chronic mental illness.


OVERVIEW: Respondent agency obtained termination of appellants' parental rights with respect to their six-year-old child. Trial court found that appellants were incapable of meeting the child's needs due to their chronic mental illness. Appellants challenged the ruling on the grounds that necessary services failed to accommodate their handicap and that their parental rights were terminated solely because of their disability, in violation of state and federal handicap and discrimination statutes. They also raised various due process claims. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling. There was little likelihood that conditions would be remedied, continuation of the parent-child relationship diminished the child's prospects for early integration into a stable and permanent home, and termination was in the best interests of the child. The trial court properly based its determination on requirements in Wash. Rev. Code §§ 13.34.180(1)-(6). The court rejected appellants' claims that there was unlawful discrimination based on mental capacity and that there was a denial of due process, as statutes protecting those with handicaps did not prevent termination of parental rights when appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the termination of appellants' parental rights, as requested by respondent agency, due to appellants' chronic mental illness which rendered them incapable of caring for their six-year-old child, whose best interests were at stake.

 

1291 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


City of Tacoma v. Franciscan Found.


No. 23107-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


94 Wn. App. 663; 972 P.2d 566; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 422; 75 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P45,849



March 5, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed from the order of Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which granted summary judgment for defendant hospital in plaintiff's suit for declaratory judgment that it had the authority to enforce the employment discrimination provisions of Tacoma, Wash., Mun. Code ch. 1.29, against defendant religious nonprofit organization.


OVERVIEW: Defendant hospital was owned and operated by a religious nonprofit organization. Two of its employees filed separate charges with plaintiff city's human rights department alleging religious, disability, race, and national origin discrimination under Tacoma, Wash., Mun. Code ch. 1.29. Defendant challenged plaintiff's jurisdiction to enforce its ordinance against it because defendant was exempt from Washington's Law Against Discrimination, Wash. Rev. Code § 49.60.040(3). Thereafter, plaintiff filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant. Both parties moved for summary judgment. The trial court granted defendant's motion. The court affirmed summary judgment for defendant. Under their constitutionally granted police powers, cities could enact ordinances prohibiting the same acts state law prohibited as long as the city ordinance did not conflict with the general laws of the state. In this case, state law expressly exempted religious nonprofit groups from civil actions for employment discrimination. Accordingly, plaintiff was without authority to enforce its ordinance against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for defendant, holding plaintiff did not have authority to enforce its ordinance against defendant because plaintiff's ordinance conflicted with Washington's Law Against Discrimination, which expressly exempted religious nonprofit groups from civil actions for employment discrimination.

 

1292 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pastrana


No. 22467-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


94 Wn. App. 463; 972 P.2d 557; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 427



March 5, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended March 16, 1999. [As amended by order of Court of Appeals May 21, 1999.] Reported at: 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 1026.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which convicted him of first-degree murder by extreme indifference and two counts of first-degree reckless endangerment as a result of his firing one shot at a car and killing one of the three occupants.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder by extreme indifference and two counts of first-degree reckless endangerment as a result of his firing one shot at a car and killing one of the three occupants. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury on the lesser included offense of manslaughter, because defendant acted with much more that mere recklessness when he fired a gun at an occupied vehicle on a major freeway ramp in heavy traffic when it was dark outside. Defendant manifested an extreme indifference to human life and created a grave risk of death, conduct that fit only the first-degree murder statute, not manslaughter. The evidence was sufficient to support the first-degree murder conviction, because defendant killed an unintended victim and jeopardized the lives of others. The first-degree murder statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.030(1)(b), was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to him, because defendant should have known that his conduct created a grave risk of death and manifested an extreme indifference to human life. Double jeopardy did not bar defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction, because the trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury on the lesser included offense of manslaughter, the evidence was sufficient to support the first-degree murder conviction, the first-degree murder statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant, and double jeopardy did not bar defendant's convictions.

Diehl v. Mason County


No. 22540-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


94 Wn. App. 645; 972 P.2d 543; 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 429



March 5, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Subsequent appeal at Diehl v. Growth Mgmt. Hearings Bd., 118 Wn. App. 212, 75 P.3d 975, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1878 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged an order from the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington), which affirmed the Western Washington Growth Management Hearings Board's invalidation of appellant's comprehensive growth management plan for failure to comply with several requirements of the Growth Management Act, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 36.70A.010 -.902.


OVERVIEW: Respondent citizens filed a petition with the hearings board to challenge appellant county's comprehensive growth management plan on the basis that it did not comply with the Growth Management Act (Act), Wash. Rev. Code §§ 36.70A.010-.902. The board invalidated the plan, and the superior court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that appellant violated the Act when it adopted a land use plan and development regulations which allowed for urban development in rural areas, failed to prevent sprawl, failed to maintain the rural nature of rural areas, allowed for non-resource based industry in rural areas, and failed to properly size urban growth areas to accommodate population projections. The court found that the board properly presumed the validity of the land use plan and development regulations, but that respondents presented evidence to overcome that presumption. The court determined that appellant failed to meet its burden of proving vagueness beyond a reasonable doubt, because the statute clearly applied to appellant's conduct and appellant failed to point to any specific language in the Act to support its argument that the Act was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the invalidation of appellant county's growth management plan, because the plan violated the Growth Management Act (Act), respondent citizens overcame presumption of validity, and appellant failed to produce evidence to support its argument that the Act was unconstitutionally vague.
