State v. Pickenpaugh


No. 39873-3-I consolidated with 39874-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1421



October 5, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Skagit County. Docket No: 96-1-00280-1. Date filed: 12/09/96. Judge signing: Hon. Michael E. Rickert.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury in the Superior Court of Skagit County, Washington, of felony violation of a no-contact order, assault, burglary, and stalking, and entered a deadly weapon special verdict on the assault charge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on his claim of self-defense. The court found that defendant precipitated the ensuing violent encounter, and did not, by his words or conduct, give any sign that he intended to withdraw or abandon the encounter or his aggressive conduct. Thus, there was no evidence to support defendant's request for a self-defense instruction. Defendant also challenged his conviction for felony violation of a no-contact order, arguing that he did not commit the underlying felonies. The court noted that the argument misperceived the elements of the offense. In order to convict defendant, the State was required to prove that he knowingly violated the no-contact order, and the evidence established the required elements. Defendant next contended that the stalking statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.110(1), was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague, and violated due process requirements. Identical arguments were recently rejected by the supreme court. Defendant's final contention was the 24-month deadly enhancement to his sentence was unlawful. The supreme court had rejected identical arguments.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DCR, Inc. v. Pierce County


No. 21416-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


92 Wn. App. 660; 964 P.2d 380; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1412



October 2, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied April 3, 2000, Reported at: 529 U.S. 1053, 120 S. Ct. 1553, 146 L. Ed. 2d 459, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2385. Petition for Review Denied May 5, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1030, 980 P.2d 1283, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 344.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an adult entertainment corporation and a dancer, sued challenging the constitutionality of Pierce County, Wash., Code ch. 5.14 (1994). They appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which dismissed their lawsuit on defendant county's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance, among other things, required all dancing to occur on a platform raised at least 18 inches from the floor and no closer than 10 feet to any patron. Pierce County, Wash., Code § 5.14.190(H) (1994). Pierce County, Wash., Code § 5.14.190(K), (L) (1994) prohibited direct tipping. The appellate court held that ch. 5.14 was content-neutral and satisfied a substantial governmental interest. The proximity of table dancing was not constitutionally protected expression. The 10-foot rule was narrowly tailored. The licensing scheme of ch. 5.14 provided a reasonable and definite time limit on the county's discretion to issue a license to an erotic dance studio.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Miller


No. 21549-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


92 Wn. App. 693; 964 P.2d 1196; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1763



October 2, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied April 6, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1023, 980 P.2d 1282, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 220. As Amended by Order of the Appellate Court December 11, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1755.


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion was originally published at: 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1411.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in Superior Court of Clark County (Washington) for attempted theft of a firearm and third degree assault.


OVERVIEW: The increase in the seriousness level for theft of a firearm in Initiative 159 was valid because the crime was fairly included within the legislative title. Theft of a firearm was by definition the act of arming oneself, and the increased penalty for the crime was fairly included with the restrictive title. Defendant was not prejudiced by the trial court's refusal to dismiss all charges following a finding of prosecutorial vindictiveness. Substantial evidence supported the trial court's determination that defendant's confession was voluntary. Although there was conflicting testimony, a police officer's testimony was substantial evidence that supported the trial court's determination that the confession was voluntary. Evidence was sufficient to establish intent to deprive an officer of his weapon where the evidence showed that the defendant tried to take an officer's gun from him. The trial court erred in calculating the defendant's offender score because theft of a firearm and third degree assault constituted the same criminal conduct.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed but the case was remanded for resentencing.

Matthews v. Wenatchee Heights Water Co.


No. 17184-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL NINE


92 Wn. App. 541; 963 P.2d 958; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1398



October 1, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied May 5, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1029, 980 P.2d 1284, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 330.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shareholder filed an action against defendants private water companies and reclamation district in the Superior Court of Chelan County (Washington) to set aside the companies' dissolutions. The trial court granted the district's motion for summary judgment and the shareholder appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held the district had not violated the Washington Constitution's prohibition against a municipal corporation owning assets of a private corporation, nor had it unconstitutionally deprived the shareholder of voting rights. The shareholder argued on appeal that the district's ownership of stock in the two private water companies violated Wash. Const. art. VIII, § 7, and, because the district's stock holdings were illegal, it could not vote as majority shareholder to dissolve the water companies. The court held that a public irrigation district did not fall within the definition of municipal corporation for the purposes of Wash. Const. art. VIII, § 7. The term "municipal corporation" was limited to its strict and proper meaning, and therefore excluded quasi-public corporations with limited purposes, such as irrigation districts. The District then did not violate Wash. Const. art. VIII, § 7 by holding stock in the two water companies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1340 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bennett


No. 41527-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


92 Wn. App. 637; 963 P.2d 212; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1334



September 14, 1998, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found that he had failed to pay restitution for an earlier guilty plea of taking a motor vehicle without permission. The juvenile court modified the disposition over defendant's objection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to taking a motor vehicle without permission. He was a juvenile at the time and he was ordered to pay restitution. During the pendency of the court's action the juvenile code was amended allowing extension of a juvenile court's jurisdiction, for the purpose of enforcing restitution for up to ten years. Defendant challenged the retroactive application arguing that as a punitive measure it was unconstitutional and violative of his rights to due process. The court affirmed, holding that the juvenile code was to be liberally construed in favor of restitution. Further, because the code allowed extension only for purposes of restitution, there was no violation of due process. The retroactive application did not deprive defendant of a vested right; he had been ordered to pay restitution, and thus, he was being deprived of nothing by an extension. Since the court extended its authority for restitution purposes only, the retroactive amendment did not offend due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the juvenile court which extended the time beyond which the defendant could be held responsible for restitution, as per the amended legislation. The legislation applied retroactively.

State v. Kinchen


No. 39117-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


92 Wn. App. 442; 963 P.2d 928; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1341



September 14, 1998, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) of two counts of unlawfully imprisoning his children in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.40.040.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sons had behavioral problems. Defendant installed numerous locks throughout their apartment, restricting the boys' access to doors, kitchen cabinets, and the bathroom. The boys did have access to a phone and were able to exit the apartment through a window. The state charged defendant with two counts of unlawful imprisonment and two counts of assault, based on the boys' allegations. A jury convicted defendant of unlawful imprisonment. The court determined that the trial court abused its discretion in admitting 31 photographs of the kitchen in the apartment, because the photos were predominantly of several padlocked kitchen cabinets, the refrigerator, and the kitchen counter, and the prejudicial effect of the photographs substantially outweighed their probative value.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of unlawfully imprisoning his children and remanded the case for retrial.

Purse Seine Vessel Owners Ass'n v. State


No. 21923-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


92 Wn. App. 381; 966 P.2d 928; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1331



September 11, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review Denied May 5, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1030, 980 P.2d 1284, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 347.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, vessel owners association and fishers, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which declined to grant them declaratory and injunctive relief against respondent state fish and wildlife department. Appellants filed the action which alleged that the department's decision not to close treaty herring fisheries while closing the non-treaty fisheries violated Wash. Rev. Code § 75.56.030.


OVERVIEW: The department did not authorize non-treaty spawn-on-kelp fisheries for a season in the interest of conservation. Appellants sought declaratory and injunctive relief, which was denied by the trial court. On appeal they claimed that the department's decision violated § 75.56.030. The court affirmed the judgment below, holding that the taking of fish was not a vested or natural property right. Non-treaty fishers were entitled to their fair share of fish, but state conservation interests were paramount to their commercial interests. The department had broad police powers to manage fish resources within state borders. Unless preempted by federal law, the state, through the department, regulated fish resources with ultimate control as to whether any fish whatsoever were taken. In addition, under § 75.08.012 the department was permitted to allow a fishery only if it did not impair the resource. Under the state Administrative Procedure Act, § 34.05, substantial weight was given to the department's actions. Because the department action here was based on conservation-related cautions given by its technical experts, its action was not arbitrary or capricious and was, therefore, upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing appellants' complaint that sought declaratory and injunctive relief from the department's decision to close non-treaty fisheries while leaving treaty fisheries open.

Thaler v. Child Protective Servs.


No. 39072-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1320



September 8, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 92 Wn. App. 1020.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-2-29937-9. Date filed: 06/26/96. Judge signing: Hon. James W. Bates Jr.



DISPOSITION: Portion of judgment awarding economic damages affirmed and awards of punitive damages and attorney fees reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father filed an action against petitioner state and caseworkers, on behalf of himself and his minor child, whom he was accused of sexually abusing. The father sought damages for negligent investigation of the abuse claims, violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, fees, and costs. The Superior Court of King County (Washington) dismissed the minor's claim without prejudice and entered judgment in favor of the father. The parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the state argued that (1) it did not owe a duty to the father to conduct a non-negligent investigation; (2) it was error to deny its motion for summary judgment on the negligent investigation claim; and (3) it was not liable for the actions of the therapist that evaluated the minor. The father challenged the dismissal of the minor's claim. As to the father's non-negligent investigation claim, the court rejected the state's argument that there was no cause of action for negligent investigation in favor of a parent accused of child abuse. The court found that the state failed to cite any persuasive authority to establish that child protective services had no duty to the father to conduct a non-negligent investigation. As to the father's § 1983 claims, the court determined that he failed to establish that the caseworkers' conduct violated a clearly established statutory or constitutional right of which a reasonable person would have known. Thus, the caseworkers were entitled to judgment on this issue, and the father was not entitled to punitive damages. Finally, the father was not entitled to attorney fees as the prevailing party in his § 1983 claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of punitive damages and attorney fees in favor of the father in his claim that the state and the caseworkers violated § 1983 by negligently investigating the claim of sexual abuse against the father. The court found that there was no evidence that the caseworkers violated § 1983. The court affirmed the grant of economic damages in favor of the father.

State v. Contreras


No. 21591-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


92 Wn. App. 307; 966 P.2d 915; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1301



September 4, 1998, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was originally arrested for obstructing a law enforcement officer when he refused to cooperate with a vehicle prowl investigation. During a search incident to arrest, officers discovered methamphetamine in defendant's pocket. Defendant claimed that the officers' handcuffing and placing him in the patrol car constituted an unconstitutional seizure, as they lacked a reasonable and articulable suspicion that he was involved in criminal activity until after they seized him. The appellate court held that the facts created a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity where the officers received a report of a possible vehicle prowl of a white car by an unidentified male and within five minutes, one officer found defendant sitting in a white car. Defendant's location in the vehicle, his suspicious and uncooperative behavior, coupled with the report of the vehicle prowl, justified the officers' investigatory stop. Defendant's refusal to put his hands up and to exit the vehicle, and giving false information, hindered and delayed the officers' investigation of a possible vehicle prowl and were sufficient to support an arrest for obstructing a law enforcement officer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1345 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


City of Bellevue v. Lorang


No. 38975-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


92 Wn. App. 186; 963 P.2d 198; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1260



August 31, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied May 5, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1027, 980 P.2d 1280, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 314.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of telephone harassment in violation of Bellevue, Wash., City Code § 10A.84.090(A). On appeal, defendant raised the issue, for the first time, as to whether the ordinance violated the free speech provisions of the First Amendment or Wash. Const. art. I, § 5, by seeking to prohibit the use of "profane" language.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the facial validity of an ordinance that defined telephone harassment as making a telephone call to another with intent to disturb, embarrass, harass, intimidate, threaten, or torment such person, using any lewd, lascivious, profane, indecent, or obscene words or language, or suggesting any lewd or lascivious act; or without purpose of legitimate communication. On appeal, the court held that while content-based regulations on speech were presumptively invalid, certain categories of speech, however, could be restricted, such as the lewd and obscene, the profane, the libelous, and the insulting or "fighting" words, because those by their very utterance inflicted injury or tended to incite an immediate breach of the peace. The court found that that "profane" had both anti-religious and secular meanings and that while anti-religious speech could not be proscribed, profanity under the secular usage of "vulgar or coarse" language could be restricted. The court held that whenever possible it would construe an ordinance to uphold its constitutionality, so it gave the term "profane" its secular meaning and directed that juries should be instructed as to that meaning.


OUTCOME: The court held that any failure of the trial court to instruct the jury on the secular meaning of "profane" was harmless error. The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant of telephone harassment.

State v. Harris


NO. 38824-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1277



August 31, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 92 Wn. App. 1013.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 96-1-00126-5. Date filed: 06/04/96. Judge signing: Hon. Richard J. Thorpe.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which, following a jury trial, convicted him of second degree robbery and sentenced him, as a persistent offender, to life without possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another man robbed a store, taking cash and food stamps. On appeal, the court ruled that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for second degree robbery. However, the court held that the trial court abused its discretion by admitting into evidence defendant's prior conviction for first degree escape as an unnamed felony for the purpose of impeaching defendant's credibility. The trial court erred when it substituted admission of the felony as unnamed for the required Wash. R. Evid. 609(a)(1) balancing of the probative value of admitting the evidence against the resulting prejudice to defendant. The trial court also erred by failing to excise a portion of defendant's taped statement to police, thus admitting improper character evidence without engaging in an Wash. R. Evid. 404(b) analysis. The court concluded that the cumulative effect of the two erroneous evidentiary rulings required reversal of defendant's conviction. The court applied a harmless error analysis and held that the untainted evidence was not so overwhelming as to necessarily lead to a finding of guilt of second degree robbery.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had convicted defendant of second degree robbery, and remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Cooper


No. 40458-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1280



August 31, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied April 6, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Wash. LEXIS 213. Reported in Table Case Format at: 92 Wn. App. 1015.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 96-1-05912-5. Date filed: 03/13/97.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of conviction of second degree assault entered by the Superior Court of King County (Washington) upon a jury verdict and the sentence imposed under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act.


OVERVIEW: The state presented evidence that defendant's attack on the victim was unprovoked, while defendant claimed self defense. The trial court gave the jury an aggressor instruction. No objection was made. Defendant was convicted of second degree assault. Under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA), the trial court imposed a sentence of life in prison without possibility of parole. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. First, the court held that the use of the aggressor instruction did not constitute a manifest error of constitutional magnitude or establish ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant failed to show prejudice from the use of the instruction. Defendant either acted in self-defense or was the aggressor. The aggressor instruction could not have changed the jury's decision. Moreover, any error in instructing the jury was harmless. The jury would have reached the same result without the instruction. Next, the court held that life sentence without parole was not disproportionate to the crime and was not cruel and unusual punishment. Finally, the court held that application of the POAA did not violate prohibitions against ex post facto laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction of defendant of second degree assault entered by the trial court upon a jury verdict and affirmed the life sentence imposed by the trial court.

In re Personal Restraint of Metcalf


No. 38546-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


92 Wn. App. 165; 963 P.2d 911; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1290



August 31, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] [As amended by order of the Court of Appeals November 2, 1998.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Changing Opinion November 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1539. Certiorari Denied June 24, 1999, Reported at: 527 U.S. 1041, 119 S. Ct. 2405, 144 L. Ed. 2d 803, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 4515.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed a writ of mandamus and a personal restraint petition challenging two statutes that mandated deductions from money received by prisoners, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 72.09.111, 72.09.480, and seeking to withdraw his guilty plea. The Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) dismissed the writ and transferred the petition to the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner challenged the statutory deductions on a number of federal and state constitutional grounds. The appellate court elected to reach the merits of the federal claims even though his claims were already determined in a prior federal class action proceeding. The court concluded that the statutes were remedial and, thus, constitutional. The court held that: (1) the prisoner's procedural due process rights were not violated because he challenged a legislative enactment and the legislative process provided all the process due; (2) his substantive due process rights were not violated because the deductions were rationally related to legitimate government interests; (3) the deductions had a remedial purpose and were not so punitive to transform them into a criminal penalty; (4) Wash. Rev. Code § 72.09.111 did not violate the single subject rule of Wash. Const. art. II, § 19; (5) an amendment to Wash. Rev. Code § 72.09.111 did not violate the scope and object rule, Wash. Const. art. II, § 38, because it only modified and added new deductions; and (6) the statutes were not special legislation in violation of Wash. Const. art. II, § 28.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the prisoner's personal restraint petition.

 

1349 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garcia


No. 37696-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1864



August 24, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of a trial court (Washington), which convicted him of attempted first degree robbery, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.56.190 and Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.28.020, and sentenced him to life without parole under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA).


OVERVIEW: Defendant told a bus passenger to give him his jacket. The passenger refused, and defendant proceeded to punch him. A bus driver ejected defendant from the bus, and defendant fled the scene without the jacket. Thereafter, defendant was convicted of first degree robbery and sentenced to life without parole under the POAA. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that sufficient evidence supported defendant's conviction because the use of force while attempting to take personal property from the passenger was sufficient to establish intent to take the jacket. Further, defendant's conduct was a substantial step towards the commission of the robbery and corroborated his intent to take the jacket. Moreover, defendant's sentence under the POAA was proper because, the people through an initiative, could rationally conclude that an attempt to commit a violent crime was serious enough to be included in the category of "most serious offenses." Thus, the POAA did not violate Washington's Equal Protection Clause. Finally, defendant's sentence was not cruel and unusual because repetition of criminal conduct aggravated the guilt of the last conviction and justified a heavier penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted first degree robbery and his sentence of life without parole.

Wozny v. State


No. 22035-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1250



August 21, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 92 Wn. App. 1007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 95-2-03808-2. Date filed: 05/15/97. Judge signing: Hon. Paula K. Casey.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gun owners sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee State of Washington in an action by the gun owners for a declaration that state law did not prohibit machine gun ownership after the United States Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, and Firearms (ATF) denied the gun owners' application for permits to obtain machine guns.


OVERVIEW: The gun owners applied to the ATF for a transfer permit to obtain machine guns for personal use. The ATF denied the application. The gun owners filed a complaint seeking a declaratory judgment that state law did not prohibit machine gun ownership and possession and that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.190 was unconstitutional. Summary judgment was granted to the state. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that before declaratory relief could be appropriate under the Washington Declaratory Judgment Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 7.24 et seq., that there had to have been a justiciable controversy. The court held that the authority to review federal agency decisions was conferred solely on the federal court, depriving the state court system of jurisdiction. The court concluded that there was no justiciable controversy and summary judgment was properly granted to the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the state.

State v. Mendoza-Espinoza


No. 14031-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL EIGHT


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1240



August 20, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 92 Wn. App. 1005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Chelan County. Docket No: 93-1-00535-1. Date filed: 05/04/94. Judge signing: Hon. Ted W. Small Jr.
State v. Mendoza-Espinoza, 92 Wn. App. 1005, 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 2617 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Chelan County (Washington), in which he was convicted of first degree kidnapping, attempted first degree kidnapping, first degree burglary, delivery of marijuana, possession of marijuana with intent to deliver, felon in possession of a firearm, and attempting to elude a pursuing police vehicle. Enhancements and exceptional sentences for the marijuana convictions were imposed.


OVERVIEW: Three juveniles burglarized defendant's residence and removed, in part, a safe with five kilograms of marijuana and cash. Defendant tracked down the juveniles, beat them, drove them against their will to different locations, and threatened them. On defendant's appeal from his convictions, the court affirmed. The court held that the civil forfeitures and criminal trial did not constitute double jeopardy. The evidence supported the kidnapping and attempted kidnapping charges because defendant's criminal purpose was readily inferred and he had taken substantial steps demonstrating his intent to kidnap. Defendant's consecutive sentences were proper under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.400(1)(b) because the acts of kidnapping and attempted kidnapping were serious violent offenses. Defendant's single subject contentions pursuant to Wash. Const. art. II, § 19 were meritless because Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.310's title was not inquired into where its amendatory provisions simply revised an existing law. The trial court's imposition of exceptional sentences did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment and was warranted given the amount of drugs involved and defendant's level of sophistication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. Burton


No. 15249-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


92 Wn. App. 114; 960 P.2d 480; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1241



August 20, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART. DO NOT CITE UNPUBLISHED PORTION. SEE RAP 10.4(h).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Yakima County (Washington), which convicted defendant of robbery and which sentenced defendant to life without parole under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA) after admitting defendant's prior robbery convictions. Defendant claimed the prior convictions on plea of guilty were facially unconstitutional and as such, did not support persistent offender status.


OVERVIEW: During sentencing for defendant's robbery conviction, the trial court admitted defendant's prior robbery convictions on plea of guilty and sentenced defendant to life without parole, pursuant to the POAA. Upon review, defendant claimed that the two prior convictions were facially unconstitutional and as such, could not support persistent offender status. In affirming the sentence, the trial court rejected defendant's contention that the due process requirements imposed by Wash. Const. art. I, § 3 were more protective than those of the federal constitution. After rejecting defendant's contention, the court held it could not determine the constitutionality of defendant's prior guilty pleas from the face of the guilty plea form.


OUTCOME: In affirming a judgment which convicted defendant of robbery and which sentenced defendant to life without parole under the POAA after admitting defendant's prior robbery convictions, the court the prior convictions on plea of guilty were not facially unconstitutional.

 

1353 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Book City v. City of Spokane


No. 16401-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL EIGHT


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1234



August 18, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 92 Wn. App. 1004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 93-2-06099-2. Date filed: 01/06/97. Judge signing: Hon. Michael E. Donohue.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an owner of two adult businesses that operated panoram booths, challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which upheld the constitutionality of respondent city's ordinance that regulated the operation of panoram booths for the exhibition of adult motion picture films. On appeal, the owner contended that the ordinance violated the constitutional protection afforded speech by Wash. Const. art. I, § 5.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted a series of regulations, Spokane, Wash., Municipal Code §§ 10.08.090(H), 10.08.100(D), § 10.08.110(A), 10.08.110(C), which established line of sight, illumination, and clear glass requirements for every panoram booth that showed adult movies. The owner's constitutional challenge to the regulations failed and on its appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the ordinance regulated speech and implicated Wash. Const. art. I, § 5. However, the challenged provisions were designed to combat the undesirable secondary effects associated with the operation of the booths and thus served a compelling state interest. The challenged regulations were content-neutral and narrowly tailored time, place, and manner restrictions that satisfied the requirements of the Washington Constitution. Spokane, Wash., Municipal Code § 10.08.100(D), which required that the interior of all panoram booths be visible by direct line of sight to persons in an adjacent room, was not so vague that persons of common intelligence had to guess at its meaning and would differ as to its application. The owner was not entitled to attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 because it did not prevail.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which upheld the city's ordinance.

Spokane Arcade v. City of Spokane


No. 15679-6-III, No. 15680-0-III, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1237



August 18, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 92 Wn. App. 1004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 95-2-02795-9. Date filed: 03/26/96. Judge signing: Hon. Neal Q. Rielly.
Spokane Arcade, Inc. v. City of Spokane, 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1238 (Wash. Ct. App., Aug. 18, 1998)
Spokane Arcade, Inc. v. City of Spokane, 92 Wn. App. 1004, 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 2614 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Ordinance is unconstitutional on its face because it fails to provide for mandatory stay pending review of license suspension and revocation. Criminal conviction disqualification provision constitutes unconstitutional prior restraint. Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, arcade and video businesses, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which held that Spokane, Wash., Ordinance C-31261 as codified in Spokane, Wash., Mun. Code § 10.08 was constitutional, in an action against appellees, hearing examiner and city, after they were denied licenses to operate adult entertainment businesses.


OVERVIEW: Appellants operated adult bookstores and video arcades. They had previously challenged the constitutionality of the adult arcade licensing ordinances, and the city had adopted a new ordinance. Appellants applied for licenses under the new ordinance, but their applications were denied. An administrative hearing resulted in the denials being upheld because appellants had previously been convicted of interstate transportation of obscene material and were therefore ineligible to obtain a license. Appellants sought review, alleging that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court held that the statute was constitutional, and appellants sought review. The court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional, and remanded for determination of attorneys fees to appellants. The criminal conviction disqualification provision constituted unconstitutional prior restraint because there was no showing that an applicant's past criminal convictions were directly related to his qualifications to operate an adult entertainment business. That portion of the ordinance could not be severed from the remaining act, so the ordinance in its entirety was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional and remanded for determination of appellants' attorney's fees, in an action brought by appellants that challenged its constitutionality after they were denied licenses to operate adult entertainment businesses.

State v. Barrett


NO. 41032-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1151



August 3, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-1-00599-6. Date filed: 07/14/97. Judge signing: Hon. Ann Schindler.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted of first degree assault while armed with a deadly weapon in the King County Superior Court (Washington), after the court denied the defendant's motion to dismiss. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant, who was 17 years old, told police he was 18. He was charged in adult court with second degree assault. The charge was later amended to first degree assault. The defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to dismiss because he should have been charged in juvenile court, and therefore, the adult court had no jurisdiction. The court of appeals disagreed. The case was filed in adult court only because the prosecutor believed the defendant's numerous representations that he was an adult. Before the defendant corrected that misunderstanding with proof of his true age, the State amended the information to charge a serious violent offense. Therefore the adult court properly exercised its original jurisdiction over the amended charge without requiring the State to refile or obtain a decline decision by the juvenile court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Calderwood


No. 20908-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1130



July 31, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 91 Wn. App. 1063.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pacific County. Docket No: 96-1-00059-9. Date filed: 06/28/96. Judge signing: Hon. Joel M. Penoyar.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Pacific County (Washington), which, based on a jury verdict, convicted him of child molestation in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction of child molestation in the first degree and remanded the case to the trial court. The court held: (1) that the trial court committed error when it admitted into evidence defendant's prior child molestation convictions for impeachment purposes because it had failed to consider a factor in its weighing of the probative value versus the prejudicial effect, the age and circumstances of defendant; (2) that there was a reasonable probability that the improper admission of the prior convictions prejudiced the jury against defendant because the prior convictions presented the only impeachment evidence disputing defendant's credibility; (3) that, although the trial court erred in allowing the child's parents and a police officer to testify about the child's prior hearsay statements, the error was harmless because the testimony was merely cumulative; and (4) that the trial court did not err in considering defendant's prior convictions for purposes of an enhanced sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of child molestation in the first degree and remanded the case to the trial court.

 

1357 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Manke Lumber Co. v. Diehl


No. 21438-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


91 Wn. App. 793; 959 P.2d 1173; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1134



July 31, 1998, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Mason County Community Development Council members (MCCDC) and the Western Washington Growth Management Hearings Board, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington), which reversed the Board's decision in an appeal brought by respondent intervenor. The sole issue on appeal was the validity of the Board's reversal of appellant county's designation of forest lands of long-term commercial significance (LTCFL).


OVERVIEW: To comply with the Growth Management Act (GMA), Wash. Rev. Code §§ 36.70A.010-902 (1990), the county engaged in a two-year planning process ending with the adoption of Mason County, Wash., Ordinance 77-93, an Interim Resource Ordinance (IRO) designating LTCFL. On appeal, the court affirmed the superior court's judgment reversing the Board's finding that the IRO failed to comply with the GMA. The Board's order was not supported by sufficient evidence to overcome the IRO's presumption of validity or to support the Board's finding that the county improperly established a desired outcome and then developed criteria to support that outcome. The Board misinterpreted the GMA in concluding that the county could not establish a minimum parcel size when designating LTCFL and that property tax classification was an improper criterion. The Board's finding that property was unjustifiably excluded from designation was not supported by substantial evidence in light of the whole record. MCCDC failed to identify any parcel that was improperly excluded. While the superior court in part usurped the Board's role of determining GMA compliance, it properly remanded to the Board for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's ruling, reversed the Board's finding of non-compliance, and remanded to the Board for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

Johanson v. DSHS


No. 20428-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


91 Wn. App. 737; 959 P.2d 1166; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1136



July 31, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied February 2, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1010, 978 P.2d 1099, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 103.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Department of Social and Health Services, State of Washington, appealed a decision from the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) entering judgment in favor of plaintiffs, counselor and federation, in their action challenging the constitutionality of 1993 Wash. Laws 1st Spec. Sess. ch. 24, § 204.


OVERVIEW: The counselor worked at a state-run treatment center. The federation was the exclusive bargaining representative for center's employees. The center was not certified for mentally ill, chemical abusing patients. The department decided to close the center under § 204 and privately contract for a mentally ill, chemical-abusing program. The counselor was laid off. The counselor and the federation initiated an action against the department alleging that the decision to close the treatment center for fiscal reasons was not a valid basis for impairing the collective bargaining agreement between the state and the federation. The trial court entered judgment for the counselor and the federation. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision, finding § 204 unconstitutional. The court found that the department could have taken steps that would not have impaired the agreement. The court held that the department could have trained and certified counselors at the treatment center to deal with mentally ill, chemical abusing patients. The court found that § 204 transferred civil service work to a private corporation thereby impairing the collective bargaining agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision entering judgment in favor of the counselor and the federation in their action against the department challenging the constitutionality of a statute closing a state-run treatment center.

 

1359 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Neill


NO. 40314-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


91 Wn. App. 978; 967 P.2d 985; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1818



July 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended July 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 96-1-02246-9. Date filed: 03/03/97. Judge signing: Hon. Janice B. Niemi.

Original Opinion Previously Reported at: 959 P.2d 1149, 959 P.2d 1149, 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1112.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicted defendant of bribing a police officer to avoid having his arrest paperwork processed. Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for bribery, alleging that he was entrapped. Unlike the normal entrapment case, the police officer was not advancing legitimate law enforcement objectives when he accepted defendant's bribe. The court of appeals held that the lower court properly declined to dismiss the prosecution for outrageous governmental behavior or for the few incidental references at trial to the police officer's religious beliefs. While the officer acted illegally in taking the bribe, the court of appeals upheld the lower court's instruction that merely affording defendant the opportunity to commit bribery would not be entrapment. This language was appropriate because it arose from the statutory definition of entrapment, which expressly applied to all crimes. However, the lower court's jury instruction went further, as it provided that "a reasonable amount of persuasion to overcome reluctance does not constitute entrapment." This sentence erroneously suggested that a corrupt police officer, who illegally solicited bribes from arrestees, could use reasonable persuasion. Thus, the State failed to show that this instructional error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

1360 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Humphrey


No. 39348-1-I, No. 39349-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE, DIVISION ONE


91 Wn. App. 677; 959 P.2d 681; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1080



July 20, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted February 2, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1008, 978 P.2d 1100, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 111.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants each pled guilty. They appealed from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which imposed a $ 500 victim penalty assessment. Defendants argued that the appropriate penalty assessment was $ 100, as provided for by law at the time the offense was committed. Defendants also asserted the $ 500 penalty violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws.


OVERVIEW: Defendants each pleaded guilty after the effective date of the amendment that imposed the higher fine. The appellate court held the statutory victim assessment penalty was imposed upon a conviction for a crime. It was the fact of conviction, not the fact of committing a particular crime, that triggered the assessment. Therefore, the legislatively mandated increase in that penalty did not implicate constitutional principles of due process or prohibitions against ex post facto laws, despite the fact that the increase occurred after the time each defendant committed their crimes, but before sentencing. The application of the higher assessment did not involve retroactive application of a statute. Further, the statute was remedial and procedural in nature, and did not affect vested or substantive rights. Thus, it could be applied retroactively in any event.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1361 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barnett


No. 38611-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


91 Wn. App. 671; 959 P.2d 691; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1097



July 20, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review on behalf of Mr. Barnett Denied and Petition for Review on behalf of the State of Washington Granted February 2, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1008, 978 P.2d 1100, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 112.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted him for first degree burglary and enhanced his sentence pursuant to RCW 9.94A.120(9)(a) for committing a crime while armed with a deadly weapon and imposed a one-year community placement sentence pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(9)(a) for committing a crime against a person.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice broke into a store at midnight and stole firearms, and left the scene by car. After a chase, police cornered their car, and found the stolen weapons in the trunk. The trial court convicted defendant for first degree burglary. The trial court found that defendant had committed a crime while armed with a deadly weapon, and accordingly enhanced his sentence pursuant to RCW 9.94A.310(3)(a). The trial court further found that defendant had committed a crime against a person, and thus imposed a one-year community placement sentence pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(9)(a). On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction but remanded for resentencing. The court held that the Hard Time for Armed Crime Act (Act), Wash. Initiative 159, did not violate the single subject rule of Wash. Const. art. II, § 19, because the legislative title of the Act, "increasing penalties for armed crime," clearly encompassed the subject of increasing the crime of first degree burglary to include entry in a non-residential building. The court further found, however, that the facts did not support the trial court's finding that defendant had committed a crime against a person.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment to the extent it convicted defendant, but remanded for resentencing.

 

1362 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


No. 22790-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


91 Wn. App. 621; 959 P.2d 152; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1066



July 17, 1998, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pastor sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which determined that a criminal defendant's statements to the pastor were not privileged pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 5.60.060(3) and held the pastor in contempt for refusing to provide testimony in defendant's trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's mother contacted the pastor, an ordained minister, to meet with defendant. The pastor did not know the mother or defendant, but went to defendant's apartment. The mother remained in the apartment while they met. The pastor met with defendant two other times. Defendant was charged with second degree murder and the state filed a motion to determine whether the statutory clergy privilege, Wash. Rev. Code § 5.60.060(3) applied to defendant's statements to the pastor. The trial court held the privilege did not apply. The pastor refused to answer questions and was held in contempt. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the privilege applied to defendant's statements because the pastor's religion constrained him to provide defendant with spiritual counsel and to lead defendant in confession. Defendant did not need to be a member of the pastor's church or faith. The court also held that defendant's communications to the pastor were confidential only to the extent the conversations were outside the presence of others. The court remanded with directions to grant the privilege to statements made to the pastor while defendant and the pastor were alone.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the pastor's contempt citation and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings, to determine whether statements made by defendant to the pastor were made in the presence of third parties, thereby compromising the clergy member privilege.

 

1363 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Nielsen v. Merriam


No. 40106-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1059



July 13, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 94 Wn. App. 1049.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 96-2-01419-1. Date filed: 01/17/97. Judge signing: Hon. Stanley K. Bruhn.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners filed an action in the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) against respondent adjacent owners alleging an easement over the adjacent owners' land. Both parties sought summary judgment. The trial court granted the adjacent owners summary judgment. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners owned real property. A grantor owned neighboring land. The county allowed the grantor to divide his lot on condition that he extend his private road to the landowners' property. The grantor orally agreed and the grantor's plat map cited an easement for property to the east. But before there was final approval of the extension, the grantor sold his land to the adjacent owners. The court held that the language of the grantor's plat map, while it indicated an unmarked easement, did not unambiguously evidence intent to grant an easement. Additionally, the county's imposition of the easement on the adjacent owners was ultra vires and an unconstitutional taking. Because the county sought to exact the easement as a condition to development, there had to have been a nexus between the easement and the adjacent owner's land. But the adjacent owners' land did not create the need for the easement. The landowners' property was accessible by two easements. The adjacent owners were not estopped from challenging the county's dedication on the ground of the grantor's promise. The adjacent owners made no promises to the landowners and had no notice of the promise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting the adjacent owners summary judgment in the landowners' action asserting an easement over the adjacent owners' land.

State v. Clark


No. 21750-3-II, No. 21751-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


91 Wn. App. 581; 958 P.2d 1028; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1025



July 10, 1998, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of two orders of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which authorized a probation officer to determine if defendants, two juveniles, violated probation, and suspended defendants' detention time.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile court authorized a probation officer to determine if defendants violated probation. The probation officer suspended a portion of defendants' sentences, and the State sought review. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held: (1) the issues posed were legal and did not require further factual development, and the orders challenged were final, thus, the issues were reviewable; (2) the juvenile court did not have the authority under Wash. Rev. Code §13.40.160 to suspend a sentence; and (3) the juvenile court was not permitted to delegate its discretion to the probation officer to find a probation violation and place defendants in detention.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the juvenile court, held that the juvenile court did not have the authority to suspend a sentence, and further held that the juvenile court was not permitted to delegate its discretion to the probation officer to find probation violations.

 

1365 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chinnell


No. 21882-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1030



July 10, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 94 Wn. App. 1046.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 96-1-04027-6. Date filed: 03/18/97. Judge signing: Hon. Frederick B. Hayes.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which convicted defendant of two counts of unlawful possession of a firearm in the first degree in a case brought by the State of Washington.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted of assault in the second degree and was in violation of the terms of his community supervision when the department of corrections received an anonymous tip as to his whereabouts. The officers observed defendant leave an apartment and return later. At that time, the officers gained entry and placed him under arrest. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court, in ruling on his suppression motion, applied an incorrect legal standard. The court found that the argument was not only based upon an incorrect premise, i.e., that the trial court applied an incorrect legal standard, it also was an inadequate assignment of error. Defendant next argued that the warrantless entry into the residence was not justifiable. The trial court found that the officers' belief that defendant lived at the residence was reasonable. This conclusion was supported by the anonymous tip, the officers' observations, and by their knowledge that defendant no longer lived at his previously known address. Further, there was sufficient evidence to show that defendant had constructive possession of the gun through proof of residency. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which convicted defendant of two counts of unlawful possession of a firearm in the first degree.

Burton v. Clark County


No. 20372-3-II consolidated with: No. 21866-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


91 Wn. App. 505; 958 P.2d 343; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1038



July 10, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Burton v. Clark County, 137 Wn.2d 1015, 978 P.2d 1097, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 161 (1999)
Related proceeding at Burton v. Harris, 2011 Wash. App. LEXIS 2188 (Wash. Ct. App., Sept. 20, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee county denied appellant landowner's plat unless he agreed to built a road on a portion of the property. The hearing examiner found in favor of the county, and the board of county commissioners affirmed. The Superior Court of Clark County (Washington), reversed and remanded. On remand, the hearing examiner found in favor of the landowner, the board, and the Superior Court affirmed. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: A road dead-ended at the landowner's property. There was another road which ran along the other side of adjacent property. The landowner sought approval of a plat plan. The county refused to approve the plan unless the landowner built a road which ran from the dead-end road across the front of the property up to the adjacent property. The county's plan was to eventually connect that road with the road which ran along the adjacent property. The landowner argued that the condition was a taking without just compensation. The court held that the county had to show that the condition was a valid exercise of police power by: (1) identifying a public problem the condition was meant to address; (2) showing that the proposed development would create or exacerbate the problem; (3) showing that the condition tended to solve the problem; and (4) showing that the condition was roughly proportional to the problem caused by the development. The court held that because the road would not solve the problem of lack of access to the property because the road would not connect to the existing road on the other side of the adjacent property, the condition was not a valid exercise of police power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the county and affirmed the hearing examiner's order approving the plat without the road.

 

1367 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Griffin


No. 37732-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1020



July 6, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 91 Wn. App. 1043.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-05017-2. Date filed: 11/09/95. Judge signing: Hon. Donald Haley.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted defendant of two counts of second degree robbery after three witnesses identified him from a photo montage.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought reversal of his conviction of two counts of second degree robbery. On appeal, the court reversed his convictions and remanded the case for a new trial. The court held: (1) the police photo montage procedure was impermissibly suggestive and the identifications were unreliable because all witnesses agreed that defendant was the only individual in the montage lineup whose skin color was similar to the robber's skin, and each witness testified that the only detail they remembered was the color of the robber's skin; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant's motion for an eyewitness identification expert; (3) the admission of evidence of defendant's drug addiction, although relevant to motive, was improper because it was unduly prejudicial; (4) the trial court's statement that it was "just guessing that the deliberations phase probably should not take long" was not an improper comment on the evidence because the court was only describing to the potential jurors the trial process as to the estimated length of the trial; and (5) the imposition of a life without parole sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of two counts of second degree robbery and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

State v. Holm


No. 40134-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


91 Wn. App. 429; 957 P.2d 1278; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1147



June 29, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] [As amended by order of the Court of Appeals July 22, 1998.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 2, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1011, 978 P.2d 1098, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 93. Order Granting Motion for Reconsideration In Part and Changing Opinion July 22, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1124.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted him of first degree burglary and which denied his motion to reinstate its plea offer for defendant to accept a guilty plea on a charge of second degree burglary. Defendant asserted ineffective counsel assistance and that his sentence pursuant to the Hard Time for Armed Crime Act violated Wash. Const. art. II, § 19.


OVERVIEW: The defendant alleged that his defense counsel failed to negotiate a plea to second degree burglary, which carried a standard sentence range of one to three months, compared to the 60-month sentence he received pursuant to the Hard Time for Armed Crime Act (act). The court found that, in light of all of the circumstances, the attorney's conduct in not attempting to negotiate a plea did not fall below the objective reasonableness standard. The court found that counsel took the steps necessary to provide adequate assistance, but the lack of plea bargaining was more of function of defendant's own dilatory actions than counsel's performance. In response to defendant's alleged constitutional violation based on his assertion that legislation was limited to a "single subject rule" pursuant to the Washington Constitution, the court noted that, by expanding the crime of first degree burglary to include entering or remaining in any building, not just a dwelling, while armed, the act did not go beyond the scope of its restrictive title. The court found defendant's sentence to be non-violative of the Washington Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentencing below against defendant.

Open Door Baptist Church v. Clark County


No. 22285-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 978



June 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 91 Wn. App. 1037.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 95-2-01589-5. Date filed: 07/24/97. Judge signing: Hon. Roger A. Bennett.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington), which found unconstitutional the county's zoning requirement that respondent church was required to apply for a conditional use permit. The court held that the requirement burdened its constitutional right to the free exercise of religion.


OVERVIEW: The church had been active at the same location for some time, but had never applied for a conditional use permit, as required in a rural estate zone under the county code. An administrative hearing resulted in an order that the church comply or it would be fined. The church brought an action against the county to challenge the determination and the trial court held that the ordinance was an unconstitutional burden on the free exercise of religion, under Wash. Const. art. I, § 11, and that the $ 5,500 application fee for a permit was excessive, and the county sought review. The court held that: (1) the issue was ripe for review because the administrative order was final, the issue was purely legal, and no development of facts was required; (2) the church was required to show that the ordinance had a coercive effect on the practice of religion and had not done so; (3) if application was made and a permit granted, no abridgement would exist; and (4) the county must ensure that its application fees did not burden religious worship, approach the question with flexibility, and reduce or eliminate the fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in part, in that the county zoning ordinance was not an unconstitutional infringement of the right to the free practice of religion, and affirmed the determination that required that the county adjust its application fee based upon ability of the church to pay the fee.

State v. Duffey


No. 21877-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 987



June 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied April 6, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Wash. LEXIS 269. Reported in Table Case Format at: 91 Wn. App. 1037.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 96-1-00524-8. Date filed: 04/18/97. Judge signing: Hon. William E. Howard.



DISPOSITION: Duffey's conviction of intimidating a public servant affirmed, his conviction for bail jumping reversed, and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), which convicted him of intimidating a public servant and bail jumping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that prosecutorial misconduct denied him his right to a fair trial and that the trial court erred in refusing to give a jury instruction and in refusing his testimony regarding his whereabouts and state of mind at the time he failed to appear. The court reversed the conviction for bail jumping and remanded for a new trial because the trial court's evidentiary ruling prevented defendant from presenting a meaningful defense. The ruling was based upon an incorrect legal interpretation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.76.170 because the trial court had failed to make a distinction between defendant's knowledge at the time of notification and his knowledge at the time of the required court appearance. The jury was improperly allowed to draw the inference that defendant was aware of the court date, without an understanding of all of the facts and circumstances relevant to his subjective knowledge. The court affirmed the conviction for intimidating a public servant because defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced by an improper prosecutorial remark or that the trial court abused its discretion in refusing his proposed instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's judgment of conviction for intimidating a public servant, but reversed his judgment of conviction for bail jumping and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Cruz


No. 35906-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


91 Wn. App. 389; 959 P.2d 670; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 953



June 22, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted February 2, 1999, Reported at: 137 Wn.2d 1008, 978 P.2d 1098, 1999 Wash. LEXIS 86.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) which ordered defendant sentenced to life in prison without the possibility of parole under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA). Defendant contended that POAA was invalidly enacted and was unconstitutional because it violated the doctrine of separation of powers and the guarantee of a republican form of government.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the trial court sentencing defendant to life imprisonment under the POAA, defendant argued that the sentence should be reversed because it was unconstitutionally imposed. The court held that POAA did not violate due process because when the trial court was only finding facts about defendant's criminal history and not about whether he was guilty of a crime, the preponderance of the evidence standard satisfied due process. Defendant contended that his 1975 guilty plea and rape conviction should not have been included as a strike against him because it was "washed out" under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.360(2). The court found that under the amended Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.360 the trial court should include defendant's sexual offenses because defendant had to remain crime free in order to take advantage of the "wash out" provisions. The court further noted that his life sentence under the POAA was not cruel and unusual punishment under the U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Wash. Const. art. 1, § 14 because the offenses that defendant were convicted of were violent against the victim and his sentence was the same as any defendant convicted of three most serious felonies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State ex rel. A.N.C. v. Grenley


No. 21163-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


91 Wn. App. 919; 959 P.2d 1130; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 943



June 19, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Amending Opinion and Order to Publish Opinion July 24, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1109.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state initiated proceedings to establish paternity and determine child support obligations for a minor, residing in Texas with his mother. The Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) determined that defendant father was the minor's biological father. Moreover, the court awarded attorney fees to the state under the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act (URESA), former Wash. Rev. Code § 26.21 (repealed 1994).


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined it did have jurisdiction, and the state obtained discretionary review in the appellate court, but before the trial court received the appellate court's mandate, the father filed a motion to set child support. Between the commencement of the case and its termination, the legislature repealed URESA and enacted a new uniform code, the Uniform Interstate Family Support Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 26.21. The revised act specifically allowed an award of attorney fees against an obligor, whereas the former act only referred to general costs and fees. The father argued the trial court erred by awarding attorney fees under former Wash. Rev. Code § 26.21.120 for the time prior to its repeal, for awarding attorney fees for the interlocutory review and for awarding attorney fees under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.21.325. The court held that it was not persuaded to depart from the trial court's original holding that former Wash. Rev. Code m 26.21.020 provided a basis for its award of attorney fees to the state. Thus, the court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's award of attorney fees to the state, excluding attorney fees pertaining to the interlocutory review. However, the court reversed that portion of the trial court's award granting interlocutory appeal fees. Moreover, the court denied that state's request for attorney fees on this appeal.

State v. Reece


No. 15603-6-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 940



June 18, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 91 Wn. App. 1028.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Chelan County. Docket No: 92-8-00487-5. Date filed: 04/09/96. Judge signing: Hon. Bart Vandegrift.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, pleaded guilty to several burglary counts. The Superior Court of Chelan County (Washington) ordered defendant to pay restitution and to collect restitution-extended jurisdiction to the date that defendant turned 21 years old. That same court later further extended jurisdiction over defendant for payment of restitution, thus lengthening the time to collect restitution. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In order to collect the restitution, the trial court extended juvenile jurisdiction until the date defendant would turn 21 years old. When the juvenile restitution statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.190, was amended to permit a trial court to extend juvenile jurisdiction for up to 10 years after a juvenile reached age 18, the trial court extended jurisdiction over defendant for payment of restitution until the date defendant would turn 27. This lengthened the time to collect restitution by approximately seven years. On appeal, defendant contended that the amendment to § 13.40.190 changed his punishment by inflicting a greater punishment than originally resulted from his crimes. The court affirmed. The court stated that extending juvenile jurisdiction retroactively to collect restitution did not violate the ex post facto prohibition of the Constitutions of the United States and the State of Washington because restitution was not punitive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments extending jurisdiction over defendant to extend the time to collect restitution.
